Large Quantities of Rice Transported to the Puppet State

Over Ten Thousand Bags Transported in Three Weeks

All Transshipped from Dalian Bay to Various Places

Since the September 18th Incident, China has prohibited the transportation of rice to the puppet state. The customs authorities do not allow any rice, wheat, or flour to be shipped to the northeast coast. The puppet state, lacking food, purchased it from Siam and Annam to compensate. Since the beginning of this year, the customs authorities have lifted the ban on rice exports, and the puppet state has been procuring food from Shanghai. From the 1st of this month to the present, a total of more than ten thousand bags of white rice have been shipped from Shanghai to the puppet state in the past three weeks. Because Andong and Yingkou are frozen, the rice is imported through Dalian and then transshipped to various places in the Northeast. The Dalian Steamship Company has transported the most, and the shipments are still continuing.

United General Association of Marine Engineers Crackdowns on Unlicensed Seamen

Yesterday, a Formal Document Was Submitted to the Ministry of Communications

Instructing the Maritime Affairs Bureau to Strictly Comply

According to Xin Xin She, the United General Association of Chinese Marine Engineers in the city, in order to crack down on unlicensed seamen and ensure safe navigation, submitted a formal document to the Ministry of Communications yesterday, instructing the Shanghai Maritime Affairs Bureau to strictly comply. The original text states: Shanghai is a major trading port, with the highest number of ships entering and leaving the country. However, many of the personnel in the navigation and engine departments of various ships not only do not possess certificates or apply for testing but also have crew members with certificates falsely impersonating others. For example, the Longshan vessel of the Sanbei Company, which is exporting this month, falsely used the name of Mao Jietang, who is currently serving on the Shengan vessel, to fill a position. Furthermore, the first and second engineers of the Sanjiang, Fuxing, and Daxing vessels of the Daxing Company, the second engineer of the Beitai vessel of the Beifang Company, and the chief engineer and first and second engineers of the Xinli vessel of the Xinchangtai Company all lack certificates. Such situations are too numerous to mention, and the Shanghai Maritime Affairs Bureau is aware of it but does not take action. Despite repeated requests from the association, they remain the same, allowing them to clear customs and set sail. According to the current laws and regulations of the Ministry, for the navigators and engineers who have not obtained certificates, except for those who have applied for testing within the prescribed time limit and have not yet completed the procedures, they may be temporarily allowed to serve. All others should be strictly cracked down on by the competent authorities by the end of November of last year and not allowed to serve in order to uphold the law. This has already been circulated in the past, but the Shanghai Maritime Affairs Bureau acts arbitrarily, disregarding the law, and it is difficult to shirk its responsibility. Moreover, sailing at sea involves dangerous conditions. In the event of an accident, the lives and property of many people would be lost at the hands of the bureau. Insurance companies can also refuse to pay compensation due to the employment of illegal crew members, indirectly increasing the losses of shipping merchants. The Ministry issued Instruction No. 2789 to the bureau in October of the 22nd year, stating that shipping companies continue to employ such personnel because they have lower salaries. This treats navigation as child's play and should be strictly cracked down on to ensure safety. As for the crew members who have certificates but are unemployed, it is unavoidable in the industry. If they are left idle and scattered, it would be a pity. The bureau should send letters to the marine engineers' associations, navigators' associations, and joint associations in various localities to conduct detailed investigations to find ways to resettle them. This is deeply insightful and takes all parties into consideration. If the bureau had a clear conscience and acted prudently and impartially, how could it have given others cause to criticize and create such a corrupt phenomenon? The association believes that China's maritime administration is still in its infancy, and it is impossible to allow this maritime affairs bureau, which abandons its responsibilities and exists in name only, to set a bad precedent and hinder the future development of the maritime administration. The association cherishes the maritime administration and has sympathy for it. Therefore, we have prepared a detailed document, hoping that you will examine it, conduct a thorough investigation, and strictly punish those responsible, ordering them to strictly comply with the laws and regulations to ensure safety and maintain the maritime administration.

Second Examination of Chinese and Foreign Seafarers

Held Yesterday at Wusong Merchant Marine School

Examinations to Be Held Every Three Months Thereafter

According to the Central News Agency, the Ministry of Communications' second examination for Chinese and foreign seafarers was held in the auditorium of the Wusong Merchant Marine School yesterday morning from 8:00 AM. There were more than fifty candidates. The examination period is four days. The examination subjects and schedule are as follows:

Candidates for the Examination

The examination was held in Shanghai, and the Ministry of Communications specifically designated Xu Zufan, the principal of Wusong Merchant Marine School, and faculty members Chen Shaoji, Zhu Tiansen, Liao Jingfang, and Liu Kaikun to form the examination committee. Additionally, the school's director, Guo Yuanzhen, and Li Yuncheng were hired to assist with the examination. Gao Tingzi, the director of the Ministry of Communications, who was specially appointed as the supervising commissioner, also went to the examination site yesterday to supervise the examination. There were more than fifty seafarers taking the exam, including six foreign seafarers from the Netherlands, Germany, and Norway.

Examination Schedule: The seafarer examination is scheduled for four days, from yesterday to the 27th. The examination schedule is as follows: (A) Navigators: The first day (24th), 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM, is for Chinese language, foreign language, and all personnel, regardless of the first, second, or third mate, or first, second, or third assistant mate, must take the exam. 2:00 PM to 5:00 PM, is for cargo loading, ship management, and seafarer duties. First mates can be exempt from ship management and cargo loading exams, second and third mates can be exempt from ship management exams, first assistant mates can be exempt from cargo management exams, and second and third assistant mates and first and second assistant third mates can be exempt from these two subjects. However, all must take the seafarer duties exam. The second day (25th), 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM, is for meteorology and navigation. Third mates, third assistant mates, second assistant mates, and first and second assistant third mates can be exempt from these two subjects. 2:00 PM to 5:00 PM, is for naval architecture and engine knowledge. Second assistant mates and first and second assistant third mates can be exempt from naval architecture, and third mates and below can be exempt from engine knowledge. The third day (26th), 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM, is for pilotage and compass knowledge. First mates and below can be exempt from compass knowledge. 2:00 PM to 5:00 PM, is for scientific principles and chart application. First and second mates, second and third assistant mates, third assistant mates, and second assistant third mates can be exempt from scientific principles. Second assistant mates and second assistant third mates can be exempt from chart application. The fourth day (27th) is for swimming in the morning (held at the YMCA) and oral exams and signaling in the afternoon. However, it is said that oral exams and signaling can be held at any level when there is no written exam. (B) Marine Engineers: The first day (24th), 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM, is for Chinese language and foreign language. All personnel from first engineers, first assistant engineers, second assistant engineers, and third assistant engineers to second engineers, first assistant engineers, second assistant engineers, and third assistant engineers must take the exam. 2:00 PM to 5:00 PM, is for mechanical knowledge, which must be taken by all. The second day (25th) is for marine engineering in the morning and drawing in the afternoon. The third day (26th) is for oral exams in the morning. Second assistant engineers and third assistant engineers will be tested in the afternoon from 2:00 PM. Foreign seafarers will be tested using the language of their respective countries.

Chen Shaoji Speaks: According to Chen Shaoji, the chairman of the examination committee, the purpose of the Ministry of Communications in holding this examination is to ensure the safety of seafarers. A total of 117 people were approved by the examination committee to take the examination. Forty to fifty people who registered did not take the exam, mostly because their ships were in other ports and they were unable to come to Shanghai to participate. If there is a valid reason, they will be allowed to take a supplementary examination. The Ministry of Communications plans to hold an examination every three months thereafter.

Ministry of Finance Mandates Consumers Bear Unified Tax on Cement

Construction Association and Others Petition for Exemption from Increase

Ministry of Finance Replies Yesterday, Finding It Difficult to Approve

The Shanghai Building Contractors Association and the Shanghai Construction Association previously submitted a joint petition to the Ministry of Finance because the Ministry of Finance doubled the unified tax on cement, and the member construction companies felt unable to bear the burden. They requested the Ministry of Finance to withdraw the order and continue to collect the tax at the original rate. The Ministry of Finance replied yesterday that it was difficult to approve and instructed them to persuade and encourage members to comply. The original text is recorded as follows: Having received the petition, the Ministry of Finance states that the cement tax increase was originally a last resort for the government. At a time when the national treasury is depleted and major construction projects and bandit suppression operations require funds everywhere, manufacturers should make an effort to assist. Moreover, the newly revised cement unified tax rate is uniformly increased throughout the country, and each factory bears an equal burden. Manufacturers are only responsible for collecting and paying the tax on behalf of others, and consumers will ultimately bear the tax obligation, so construction companies should not experience any particular difficulties. As for imported cement, since it must also complete customs duties, how can it be sold at a lower price? This matter concerns a general case, so the request to withdraw the order is difficult to approve. The construction companies are all deeply understanding, so please persuade and encourage them to comply. This is our sincere hope. This batch.

Ministry of Communications Explains Fee Collection Method for Foreign Language Cipher Telegrams

Cannot Imitate Domestic Cipher Telegram Fee Collection

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce previously submitted a petition to the Ministry of Communications, stating that the domestic foreign language five-letter cipher telegram fee collection was higher than international regulations and requested a reduction to benefit commerce. It has now been learned that the Chamber of Commerce received a response from the Ministry of Communications yesterday, which is recorded as follows: Having received the tele message, the Ministry of Communications states that foreign language ten-code cipher telegrams have no meaning and are difficult to pronounce. Telegraph bureau staff find it extremely difficult to transmit these telegrams, and even if the speed is reduced, there is still a risk of errors. The competent authorities of various countries' telecommunications have long discussed abolishing ten-code cipher telegrams. The Ministry also believes that this matter can improve the speed and accuracy of telegram delivery and benefit both the telegraph bureau and the public. Therefore, it has been decided to abolish domestic foreign language ten-code cipher telegrams and replace them with five-code ones when implementing the new regulations of the Madrid International Telegraph Conference this year. As for the five-code cipher telegram fee collection method, the Ministry has carefully considered it before making regulations, and there are various reasons why it cannot imitate the international cipher telegram reduction fee collection. The explanations are as follows: (1) The standards for domestic rates and international rates are fundamentally different. The standards for domestic telegram rates are fundamentally different from international telegram rates. For example, the distance between Nanjing and Peiping is roughly equal to the distance between Nanjing and Nagasaki. However, a foreign language telegram from Nanjing to Peiping only costs 20 cents per word, while one to Nagasaki costs 1.25 yuan per word. If domestic rates were set according to international standards, the current rates between Nanjing and Peiping would have to be increased by at least six times, which is not allowed. (2) Domestic foreign language five-code cipher telegrams should be charged the same as Chinese cipher telegrams to ensure fairness. Currently, domestic telegram rates for Chinese plain text are 10 cents per word for four codes, and for Chinese cipher text are 20 cents per word for four or five codes. This has been in place for a long time and has not caused any inconvenience. The new foreign language five-code cipher telegrams are composed of five Roman letters, and their rates are equal to Chinese cipher telegrams. However, the labor and materials required for transmission are more than Chinese cipher telegrams. If foreign language cipher telegrams are charged at a reduced rate according to international telegram regulations, while Chinese cipher telegrams maintain the old price, it would be unfair to the public sending cipher telegrams domestically. If, therefore, Chinese cipher telegram rates are uniformly reduced, the loss would be too great, which the current depleted telecommunications economy cannot afford. Therefore, the matter of reducing domestic foreign language cipher telegram fees may be realized when the telegram business develops and the economic situation is better, or when Chinese cipher telegram fees are reduced at the same time. However, it is not the time yet. (3) One word in a cipher telegram can replace dozens of words in plain text, and the fees are already very low. Cipher telegrams can use one word to represent dozens of words in plain language. For example, according to the ABC Telegraphic code, the word OPKAH represents "goods advised 'To be delivered free of duty and all charges' Collect duty forward but debit us with delivery charges to the nearest railway station Reference No（｜｜）," which is 27 words, not including punctuation marks. Currently, it is only charged at the rate of one word in foreign language plain text, which is very low. If it is reduced by 40% according to plain language rates, it would be too unfair to senders of plain language telegrams. (4) For the convenience of calculation and fee collection, domestic foreign language cipher telegrams need to have the same rates as plain language. The Ministry of Communications aims to simplify and streamline domestic telegram rates. For example, Chinese plain text is charged at 10 cents per word, regardless of whether it is within the province or across provinces. When Chinese cipher telegrams or foreign languages are doubled, it is convenient. If a separate fee collection method is established for foreign language cipher telegrams, domestic telegram rates will become complicated again, which is not appropriate. In short, the Ministry of Communications manages the national transportation industry and actively strives to facilitate public communication and reduce the burden on the people. In previous months, we launched inexpensive social telegrams, stipulated that incoming telegrams are free of charge, and that Arabic numbers can be used to represent numbers and telephone numbers can be used to replace telegram addresses in translated telegrams. Recently, we implemented new regulations for Chinese telegram addresses, which saves money, and reduced the price of express telegrams, which are all major measures. According to statistics, the implementation of the new regulations for telegram addresses alone will reduce government revenue by 400,000 yuan per year. The reduction in the price of express telegrams will reduce revenue by another 100,000 yuan. The Ministry's emphasis on these public interests and its efforts to facilitate communication are evident to the people. Foreigners account for the majority of users of foreign language cipher telegrams, and the new fee collection method has a minimal impact on Chinese merchants. All the reasons have been stated above. We hope that you will inform the members of the explanation in detail to avoid misunderstandings. This is most important. This batch.

After public discussion among our colleagues, everyone expressed deep admiration for Ms. Jiang's noble aspiration of offering salvation as a prominent woman from a distinguished family. However, as both our northern and southern teams are departing for the front lines without any female participants, it would be inconvenient for her to accompany the team. Moreover, Fujian Province is mountainous, with difficult roads and thorny paths. Even the relief team must venture forth at their own risk to provide disaster relief in the affected areas. How could we ask a woman to lightly attempt such a task? Should there be a need for female members to assist in the front lines in the future, we will send a special letter to request her assistance to fulfill her great ambition." We are sending this letter in reply, hoping you will convey our message and our sincere admiration.

Netherlands Restricts Import of Rattan, Willow, Bamboo, and Grass Utensils

Letter from the Netherlands Consulate

International Trade Bureau for Reference

According to the Guidance Office of the International Trade Bureau, the Bureau recently received a letter from the Netherlands Consulate in Shanghai regarding the restriction of the quantity and value of rattan, willow, bamboo, and grass utensils exported from China. The country recently promulgated new regulations that all imports from various countries to the Netherlands, such as wooden furniture, velvet, leather, electrical utensils, glass, ceramics, and utensils made of rattan, willow, bamboo, and grass, are subject to considerable import restrictions. Of the above-mentioned commodities, China has exports of wooden goods and rattan, willow, bamboo, and grass utensils. There are very few or no exports of other commodities. Only Chapter 1 of the regulations, regarding furniture, is recorded. (1) (2) are as follows: (1) Regarding furniture, (A) the import value of wooden goods or furniture decorations and their parts from various countries shall not exceed 75% of the export value of the same trade goods in any five months of 1931 and 1932; (B) the import value of bamboo, rattan, reed, and wicker products shall not exceed 75% of the average quantity value of the exporting country in any five months of 1931 and 1932; (2) the import value of coarse velvet, silk velvet, wool velvet, and other velvet fabrics and their manufactured products shall not exceed the average export

75% of the quantity value of the exporting country in any five months of 1931 and 1932.

Minutes of the Meeting of the Rickshaw Industry Association

Discussing How to Deal with the Notice of Suspending the Issuance of Licenses

The Shanghai Rickshaw Industry Association held a discussion meeting at its association in Sanminfang, Nanshi at 10 AM the day before yesterday. Because many unlicensed members came to the meeting, some even cried out for relief because the authorities had stopped issuing rickshaw licenses, and their livelihoods had been interrupted. Some棚户 only had one rickshaw, which affected their business and they appealed to the association. The association believed that these people were all poor and ordinary people, and many families relied on one rickshaw for a living. Therefore, it first ordered registration (only those who had legal licenses but were suddenly suspended this time could register), and then the standing committee members Qiu Chunshan, Yu Dajin, etc., comforted them. In the afternoon, a general meeting of representatives was convened at the association's施材部 at Sanguantang, Xieqiao. More than 200 representatives attended. Standing Committee member Qiu immediately expressed his opinions. Then, Li Jibing, Liu Qikuan, etc., reported on the process of petitioning the Chinese Taxpayers Association in the French Concession. Then, the attendees discussed and proceeded with countermeasures. The chairman put the following to a vote: (1) Submit a written request to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the Chinese Taxpayers Association in the French Concession, requesting them to find a way to supplement the donation, and attach a registration form for unemployed vehicles; (2) Re-elect the original representatives and go to the association and the French Concession Board of Directors to discuss the supplementary donation methods; (3) When necessary, request the Chinese directors and Chinese members of the French Concession Board of Directors to consider the livelihoods of the poor and provide assistance, or to mediate with the French authorities; (4) When necessary, submit a request to the Party and government agencies and groups, requesting them to uphold justice and provide assistance in negotiations; (5) Publish the unemployment and hardship of rickshaw merchants and rickshaw drivers, and hold a large petition when necessary; (6) If the above methods cannot achieve the goal, it is decided to unite the north-south city and the special zone car merchants and car drivers to unanimously assist in holding a city-wide petition and stop business altogether; (7) When necessary, elect petition representatives to go to Beijing and submit a request to the central national government and the foreign ministry to negotiate with the French authorities; (8) From now on, labor and capital should cooperate and help each other to the end. Do not stop until the purpose of supplementing the donation is achieved; (9) Organize a committee to stop donations and licenses in the French Concession, elect members, and specialize in studying the countermeasures of this case; (10) Omitted. The above proposals were unanimously passed and handed over to the association's executive committee for handling and execution. It was not until after 5 PM that the members were dispersed by the representatives. Before leaving, some people cried and left because of unemployment, which was quite sympathetic to those who heard it.

On the 19th of this month, Shen Jingen in Yangjing Town, Pudong, got married. Jincheng Grand Theatre Opens Soon

First Film Selected is Lianhua's "Life"

The long-rumored Jincheng Grand Theatre is located at the intersection of Beijing Road and Guizhou Road, with convenient transportation and a wide road in front, which is convenient for parking vehicles. The entire magnificent building has now been completed, and the interior layout has also been arranged, with the utmost luxury. There are more than 1,800 seats upstairs and downstairs, all using spring chairs and covered with floral silk seat covers. The size and style have been researched for several months and modified many times before being completed. The four walls of the theater are decorated with the best non-combustible sound-absorbing cardboard, so that the sound from the screen, even the farthest and most biased part of the theater, can be clearly heard. In addition, the theater is equipped with the latest German-made real-sound giant machine, so the sound is clearer. The color of the paint in the whole theater is elegant and pleasant, not

thick or vulgar, and there are five green glass columns in front, soaring into the sky, magnificent and beautiful, adding to the beauty. The angle of the seats is suitable, and there is no bias in the center of the focus. The whole theater is covered with wool carpets, which is beneficial for sound and magnificent. The installed cold and hot air conditioners are also the latest type. Such a high-end theater is the best in Shanghai. The price of the seats is very low in order to be popular. In short, the theater uses the latest European and American methods for equipment management and film selection, and takes the eyes and body of the Chinese people as the main point of view. It is truly the only paradise for the Chinese people in Shanghai. The first film to be launched has been carefully selected from Lianhua's best product of the past year, "Life." The film stars Ruan Lingyu and others, and the director of this film is Fei Mu, the director of "City Night." The whole film is not only technically a Lianhua honorary work, but also worth praising in terms of consciousness.

Fire on Xietu Road, Nanshi

At about 4 AM yesterday morning, the Shunxing Fried Noodles Restaurant at No. 230 Xietu Road, Nanshi, which had not yet opened, suddenly caught fire due to negligence. The fire quickly spread. The Liyuan Road Police Station in the relevant Second District immediately reported it to the fire brigades in each district to drive to the rescue and poured water with all their might, but it was too late. The Yongli Southern Goods Store and Coal Store next door, which had just opened for less than two weeks, were also completely burned down. The Xieda Cigarette Paper Store also suffered considerable losses. The long police officer on the spot took the fire starter, Ni Cheng (43 years old), a native of Tongzhou, to the station. After a preliminary interrogation, he confessed that he had rented the house from the Yuye Company at No. 273 Fangxie Road on the 20th of this month in the old calendar. The rent and tips had been paid, and it was scheduled to open the day after tomorrow. Because of decorating the facade, the carpenter left wood flowers behind, and the candle fell into the fire at night, causing misfortune.

Unveiling the Inside Story of the Thirteen Thousand Dollar Fraud Case

Wang Chung-kan Steals a Check

A Russian Forges the Signature

Regarding the case where the Mackenzie & Co. bank was defrauded of $136,688.25 by swindlers using a forged check with the signature of a manager from the British American Tobacco Company, the report from the General Police Station stated that a Russian named J. P. Afanasiev, an employee of the Pu Xi Yanghang, was suspected of being involved in the scheme and was detained at the First Special District Court for interrogation. This was previously reported. Since the Russian's arrest, the police have continued their investigation and learned that another Russian named Ignatieff was also one of the perpetrators. Ignatieff was acquainted with Wang Chung-kan (also known as Wang Hao-ran), a Chinese employee of Mackenzie & Co. from Zhejiang. Before the fraud, Ignatieff had inquired with Wang about the financial dealings between the British American Tobacco Company and Mackenzie & Co. He also asked Wang to let him see the British American Tobacco Company's checks kept in the bank. Wang complied with his request and secretly took a check that had already been paid by Mackenzie & Co. from the safe deposit box and gave it to him. Ignatieff was then able to imitate the signature and forge the check with his accomplices to obtain the large sum of money. However, after the incident, Ignatieff immediately fled and disappeared. The authorities, considering that Wang Chung-kan's irregular actions indicated collusion with the other perpetrators, sent detectives to Mackenzie & Co. yesterday to arrest Wang. Wang confessed to letting Ignatieff inspect the check. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the First Special District Court, where Judge Feng interrogated him. The police lawyer, Li Zhi-shan, explained the case and requested that Wang be detained along with the previously arrested Russian suspect. The court granted the request and ordered the defendant to be detained for further interrogation.

Kidnappers Buy a Car and Rent a Foreign-Style House Specifically for Kidnapping Tao Chang-hai

Preparations Were Made Multiple Times Between Hangzhou and Shanghai

Finally, the Abduction Took Place at the Intersection of Avenue Edward VII.

A Ransom of Five Hundred Thousand Dollars Was Initially Demanded

The Gangsters' Interrogation Continued Until Dusk Yesterday Before Adjourning

Tao Chang-hai, a local comprador for Arnhold, Karberg & Co. on North Sichuan Road, was kidnapped on the night of December 24th last year at 12:10 AM. He was returning to Shanghai from Hangzhou in his own car when he was abducted at the intersection of North Henan Road and Avenue Edward VII. He was held captive in a room on the upper floor of the gang's den at No. 91 Guling Road (North He Road). A letter demanding a large ransom was sent. The case was solved by the entire team of investigators from the Inspectorate General's Office, including Chief Inspector Lu Lian-kui, Detectives Liu Shao-kui and Feng Zhi-ming, and Police Officers Liu Jun-jie and Wu Huan-zhang, at 7:00 PM on the 13th of this month. The victim, Tao Chang-hai, was rescued, and sixteen people were arrested, including kidnappers Xiang Fei-qing, Xu A-rong, Fei Zhu-shi (a woman), and suspects Bao Zu-cai, Xu Wang-shi (a woman), and Tao Wang-shi (a woman). Three pistols, 101 bullets, glasses, iron chains, and other items were also seized. All were sent to the First Special District Court. After Tao Chang-hai detailed the events and identified the defendants, they were ordered to be remanded in custody for further proceedings. The police investigation revealed that seven of the defendants, including Bao Zu-cai, Jiang Yong-xi, Cao Nai-wen, Lu Gui-sheng, Dong Bing-you, Xu Wang-shi (a woman), and Tao Wang-shi (a woman), were not involved in the case and requested their release. This was previously reported in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Liu Yu-gui, presiding over the Second Criminal Court, continued the interrogation. The police lawyer, Wang Yao-tang, stated that during the adjournment, it was discovered that:

The Ring Leader of This Case

Was Named Chen Gui-sheng

In April of last year, Chen Gui-sheng, along with the fugitive Wang Xue-qing and defendant Fei Xiang-qing, plotted to kidnap Tao Chang-hai. Later, Chen committed another crime and was arrested by the French police and sentenced to death by the Second Special District Court. The plan was thus halted. Later, in September, Wang Xue-qing and others continued the plan with the fugitive Tao Yu-tang. Tao Chang-hai often went to Hangzhou for business, and they planned to abduct him near the Gongchen Bridge. The defendants Fei Xiang-qing, Xu A-rong, and Zhou Song-lin went to Hangzhou to wait for an opportunity to act, but due to time constraints, it was difficult to carry out the plan. (Wang Xue-qing lived at No. 3 West Main Street in that area.) They changed their strategy and returned to Shanghai in November. Tao Yu-tang and five others, including Chen De-quan, each contributed 320 yuan and made a down payment to the Pick Company to purchase a Chrysler automobile for the purpose of kidnapping Tao Chang-hai. Tao Yu-tang also arranged to rent a building at No. 91 North He Road from the Union Realty Department at No. 12 Jiujiang Road for 85 taels of silver per month, starting from the first of this month. He asked Mrs. Zhang, the owner of the Wanli Clothing Store in the French Concession, to have her son act as guarantor. The house was prepared to hold the hostage. After everything was arranged, Zhou Song-lin, Zhang Lin-sheng, Zhu Kun-shan, Fei Zhu-shi, and Xu Xue-shi moved into the house one after another. On the 23rd, Wang Xue-qing learned that Tao Chang-hai would:

Return to Shanghai from Hangzhou the Next Evening

Tao Yu-tang then notified Chen De-quan to drive the Chrysler automobile (original license plate number 4306) to the front of No. 91 North He Road and hand it over to the defendant Xu Zhao-fu, the driver, to drive to the North Railway Station. He then used black paper and white characters to change the license plate to No. 8376 and went to the intersection of North Henan Road and Avenue Edward VII. When Tao Chang-hai's car arrived, they blocked its path. Tao Yu-tang, Zhu Xiang-qing, and Xu A-rong, each holding a pistol, forbade any outcry. Tao Yu-tang rushed forward, dragged Tao Chang-hai out, and pulled him into the car. Zhu, Xu, and Tao sat next to him to watch over the hostage. On the way, they removed the fake license plate number, revealing the original number 4306, and drove directly to the gang's den, where they held the hostage on the upper floor of the side room. They put black glasses on him and used iron chains to lock his feet. They forced him to write letters to his family:

Demanding a Ransom of 500,000 Dollars

For His Release, a Total of Five Letters. An Investigation Revealed That Tao Chang-hai Wrote Only One Letter; the Rest Were Written by the Gang Using the Name Wang Tie-min (The Alias Used by Fei, Xu, and Tao). A Person Had Been Sent to Negotiate Twice Before and Received 500 Yuan. Later, on the 13th Evening, While Meeting Again at the Corner of Route Ghisoni and Avenue Haig, They Were Caught by the Police. Now, a Public Prosecution Has Been Filed Based on Article 1, Paragraph 1 of the Provisional Regulations for the Punishment of Bandits and Article 371, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Code for the Crime of Intimidation. The Letters, Iron Chains, Guns, and Ammunition Were Presented to the Court for Inspection. The Court Ordered Each Defendant to Be Interrogated Separately. Fei Xiang-qing Testified That in April of Last Year, He Met Chen Gui-sheng in Hangzhou. Chen Proposed Kidnapping Tao Chang-hai and Opening a Cangzhou Hotel. Wang Xue-qing Was Also Present. They Discussed It Once, But Chen Committed a Crime in Tianjin and Was Never Seen Again. In September, He Continued the Plan with Tao Yu-tang and Others. Chen De-quan Was Entrusted to Purchase the Automobile. I Also Contributed 320 Yuan. There Were a Total of Five People Sharing the Cost. The Car Cost a Total of 1,050 Taels of Silver. Tao Yu-tang Rented the House on North He Road for 85 Taels per Month. When Tao Chang-hai Returned to Shanghai, Wang Xue-qing Notified Us.

Tao Yu-tang Retrieved the Guns, and He, Xu A-rong, and Xu Zhao-fu Took the Self-Purchased Car. Xu, the Driver, Stopped the Car at the Intersection of North Henan Road and Avenue Edward VII. Tao Yu-tang Then Dragged the Hostage into the Car. He and Xu A-rong Sat on the Left, and Tao Sat on the Right.

The God of Wealth Resided in the Center, Driving Directly to the House at No. 91 North Henan Road. They Confined Him Upstairs. Tao Yu-tang Asked Someone to Write a Letter to the Victim's Family Demanding a Ransom, Etc. Xu A-rong Testified That in September of Last Year, He Met Fei Xiang at Baoshan Road. He Said That Tao Chang-hai Was a Comprador for Arnhold, Karberg & Co. and Had Money, So They Proceeded with the Kidnapping. Chen De-quan Handled the Purchase of the Car, and He Also Received the Registration. He Contributed a Share of 320 Yuan to Fei. He Had Planned to Kidnap the Victim in Hangzhou. Wang Xue-qing Accompanied Him, But the Hotel They Stayed In Was Not Suitable, So They Changed to Shanghai. That Night, Wang Xue-qing Notified Him. He, Tao Yu-tang, Fei Xiang-qing, and Xu Zhao-fu Went to Abduct the Victim to the Pre-Rented House and Handed Him Over to Zhou Song-lin and Zhang Lin-sheng to Guard Him. The Second Time He Contacted the Family, He Received 500 Yuan. Xu Zhao-fu Testified That He Drove for the Dala Motor Company. He Was Responsible for Driving the Car in This Incident, Going to Kidnap Tao Chang-hai and Driving to No. 91 North He Road. The Car Was Later Driven to Wuzhou Road and Returned to Chen De-quan. He Watched Over the Hostage in the East Side Room of the House at Night. Zhou Song-lin Testified That He Was Introduced by Tao Yu-tang.

He Had Also Been to Hangzhou

After the House on North He Road Was Rented, He Lived There. That Night at 11:00 PM, the Hostage Arrived. He, Xu Zhao-fu, and Zhang Lin-sheng Took Turns Guarding Him. Zhang Lin-sheng Testified That He Was Introduced by Wang Xue-qing on the First of This Month to Work as a Cook in the House at No. 91. After the Hostage Arrived, Tao Yu-tang Told Him to Guard Tao Chang-hai, From 6:00 AM to 7:00 PM, He and Zhou Song-lin Switched Shifts. Zhu Kun-shan Testified That He Used to Be a Cook at Wang Xue-qing's House at No. 3 West Main Street in Hangzhou. On December 11th of Last Year, He Came to Shanghai with Him and Went to the House at No. 91, Still Working as a Cook. That Night, Tao Yu-tang and Xu Zhao-fu Brought the Hostage. Each Time, After He Cooked the Food, He Handed It Over to Zhang Lin-sheng to Give It to Him to Eat. Fei Zhu-shi Testified That She Lived in Suzhou. She Went to Hangzhou in September of Last Year and Became Acquainted with Zhou Song-lin. Later, Tao Yu-tang Told Her to Come to Shanghai and Live Downstairs in the House.

That Night When the Hostage Arrived,

She Was Asleep and Did Not Know About the Events Upstairs. Xu Xue-shi Testified That in November of Last Year, Fei Xiang-qing's Employer Brought Her to Shanghai From Hangzhou and She Lived Downstairs at No. 91. She Did Not Know That Tao Chang-hai Was a Hostage. She Heard That He Was a Relative of Old Class Wang. She Did Not Know Anything Else. Chen De-quan Testified That He Used to Cook for a Company and Became Acquainted with Fei Xiang-qing. In September of Last Year, He Was Told to Purchase a Car on His Behalf, Not Knowing What It Would Be Used For. He Purchased a Chrysler Automobile From the Pick Company for 850 Taels. The Money Was Paid to Him in Installments of 100 or 200 Yuan at a Time. Each Share Was 320 Yuan. He Did Not Receive the Registration. He Later Learned That It Was Used for Kidnapping Tao Chang-hai. That Night, He Was Told to Drive to Guling Road and Hand It Over to Xu Zhao-fu to Transfer to North Henan Road to Abduct the Hostage. He Then Took a Rickshaw and Followed to the Location to Observe. He Did Not See the Vehicle. After a While, Xu Still Drove the Car to Shanhai Guan Road and Returned It. The Rest of His Testimony Was Evasive. The Interrogation Continued Until Dusk. Judge Liu Ordered That They Be Remanded in Custody Separately to Await Further Questioning After Summoning Witnesses.

Comparison of Bacteria in Water Tested by the French Concession Hygiene Laboratory

The Hygiene Laboratory of the Shanghai French Concession Board of Directors has released a comparison of bacteria in the Huangpu River water and the tap water in the French Concession for January 1934. The types of tests and the results are as follows: (1) Huangpu River water: 28,800 bacteria per cubic centimeter, 150,000 groups of E. coli per liter; (2) Tap water in the French Concession: 34 bacteria per cubic centimeter, 20 groups of E. coli per liter. The purification percentage is 99.93%.

Double Suicide by Poisoning at the Old Eastern Hotel

Zhou Xie-sheng and Zheng Yin-hua

Commit Suicide Due to Weak Will and Romantic Despair

Suddenly, a Couple Arrives

Yesterday afternoon, a young couple committed suicide by poisoning at the Old Eastern Hotel on Zhejiang Road, near the Samma Road. The details are as follows: Around 2:00 PM the day before yesterday, a young couple arrived at the Old Eastern Hotel and booked room number 40 on the fourth floor, paying a deposit of five yuan. The man identified himself as Wang Xie-sheng, 24 years old. The woman:

Did Not Leave Her Name. Soon after, they went out together and returned around 6:00 PM, bringing back a large amount of fruit. They ate and talked, appearing very affectionate and showing no signs of distress. Around 1:00 AM yesterday morning, they went out again and did not return to sleep until around 4:00 AM, near dawn.

Instructions to the Tea Boy Before Going to Bed

Before going to bed, they instructed the tea boy to call them after 12:00 PM, saying that they were feeling weak. When the time came, the tea boy routinely inquired whether the guests wanted to extend their stay. He knocked on the door and called out several times, but there was no response. Suspicion arose, and he forced the door open. He saw a couple embracing in bed. He felt them and found that their bodies were as cold as ice and their faces were pale. It appeared that they had committed suicide by poisoning.

Sent to the Hospital for Examination

The tea boy immediately reported to the front desk, who in turn reported to the relevant police station. Detectives rushed to the scene and transported the bodies of the man and woman to Renji Hospital in an ambulance. After examination, the doctor determined that they had committed suicide by taking opium paste. The bodies were then transferred to the morgue to await legal examination. A paper package was found in the room, filled with numerous photographs and letters, but no suicide note. The detectives took these items back to the police station for safekeeping.

Description of the Deceased's Clothing

The man was wearing a camel-colored flannel robe, wool socks, and leather shoes, with a felt hat. The woman was in her late teens, with short hair and somewhat attractive features. She was wearing a diagonally striped red cotton cheongsam, a black wool coat with a leather collar, coffee-colored silk stockings, and black velvet shoes.

The Real Names of the Man and Woman

After the incident, reporters investigated and learned that the deceased man was named Zhou Xie-sheng, 24 years old, from Suzhou. He worked as a registration clerk at Chongren Hospital on Six Ma Road, under Dr. Wu Yu-sun. He had previously been a trainee at the hospital before being promoted to this position, earning over 20 yuan per month, which was enough to live on. The woman was named Zheng Yin-hua, only 17 years old, from Ningbo. She was temporarily staying at her sister's Yongcangxiang clothing shop at No. 10 Yuren Lane on Yunnan Road. Her sister was pregnant and due to give birth soon, so she had written to Ningbo, inviting her mother to Shanghai to help with the childbirth. Yin-hua, unaccustomed to rural life, came with her mother. It had only been a month.

The Origins of Their Acquaintance

However, Shanghai was a bustling metropolis, and Yin-hua was influenced by what she saw and heard, becoming increasingly fashionable. In her free time, she often strolled along the nearby streets. One day, she happened to meet Zhou Xie-sheng. They exchanged affectionate words, fell in love at first sight, and swore a vow of love. Since then, the couple was often seen at movie theaters and amusement parks. It is said that Zhou had visited her sister's house once. Recently, due to marriage issues, they committed double suicide by poisoning.

Two Towboats of the Shanghai-Shasha Shipping Bureau Capsize

Small Boats Carrying Too Much Cargo Encounter Danger Exporting

Losses Estimated at 14,000 Dollars

Service Suspended to Handle Compensation Procedures

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, the Shanghai-Shasha Shipping Bureau, located west of the Lao Gongmao Steamboat Bureau along the Suzhou Creek bank at Penthang Lane in this city, set out three small cargo boats towed by a small steamboat on the 20th of this month. The boats were fully loaded with sugar and sundry goods. Around 3:00 AM, when the boats were sailing out of the Suzhou Creek towards the No. 1 Wharf of the Dada Company on the outer river, they were struck by a large wave and the towboat hit an iron anchor, causing two of the cargo boats to sink on the spot. The losses are estimated at 14,000 dollars. The details of the investigation are as follows:

Established Not Long Ago

The Shanghai-Shasha Shipping Bureau was established less than a year ago. The manager is Jin Hui-dong, and it was co-founded by Qiao Nian-chun, the manager of the Shanghai-Zhang Shipping Bureau, Jin Hui-dong, and merchants from Kunshan, Taicang, and other places. It operates routes from Shanghai to Kunshan, Taicang, Shuangfeng, Zhita, and Shatou. The steamboats used are in cooperation with the Shanghai-Zhang Shipping Bureau. The board of directors is located in the Wantai Sauce Garden in Taicang. It mainly transports goods from various places.

Cause of the Accident

This time, it was near the Lunar New Year, and Nanhang shops from Kunshan, Taicang, Shatou, and other places were purchasing New Year goods in Shanghai. They collectively purchased white and brown sugar, seafood, and other sundry goods from Junyi Sugar Shop and other places in this city and entrusted the shipping bureau to transport them. A total of three cargo boats were loaded and towed by a small steamboat. However, the cargo boats were very small, and the goods were divided among the three boats, totaling over 500 packages. At the same time, the shipping bureau's steamboats usually sailed on the inner river waterway of the Suzhou Creek, making navigation easier. On that day, because the Suzhou Creek was silted up and impassable, all the inner river steamboats had to take a detour via the Huangpu River. The shipping bureau thought that the New Year goods were seasonal items that could not be delayed, so they also decided to take the outer river route, hoping to deliver the goods as soon as possible.

Process of Capsizing

However, the driver lacked experience in navigating the outer river. In addition, the weather had been overcast and the tide had been high in the past few days. The tide caught the wind, making the river current even stronger. Therefore, despite venturing out, the boats were only able to reach the No. 1 Wharf of the Dada Company before being struck by a large wave. The cargo boat hit a large iron anchor, and the small boat was overloaded, causing it to sink immediately. Four crew members also fell into the river. Fortunately, police officers from the Public Security Bureau's water patrol team were stationed there. Without waiting for a call for help, they immediately drove a boat to rescue them, and they were safe. The other boat was also saved by the crew and water police. It was immediately driven back to the shipping bureau. The two boats that capsized were only lifted from the Dada Wharf that afternoon. However, the sugar cargo had already been consumed by the fish.

Losses of Over Ten Thousand

After the incident, an investigation revealed that both of the sunken boats were carrying sugar cargo loaded by Junyi, totaling 400 packages. Fortunately, one boat was saved, carrying approximately 100 packages of sugar and sundry goods, totaling 15,000 yuan. Therefore, the total losses suffered were said by people in the shipping bureau to be over 13,000 yuan. It was also learned that Junyi Sugar Shop and others had already received payment in advance. Therefore, the negotiations are being handled directly by the Nanhang shops from Shatou, Hengjing, and other places and the shipping bureau. It is said that the compensation will be based on the original price, with a certain percentage being paid. The shipping bureau will only resume operations after the compensation negotiations are completed.

The License Plate Number of the Car That Kidnapped Fan Ai-sheng Was Forged

Car Number 6539 Belongs to an American

Regarding the incident where Fan Ai-sheng, the manager of Dehe Gongji Indigo Shop and a prominent dye merchant in this city, was forcibly dragged from his hired car at the intersection of Shantou Road and Guangxi Road at 7:45 PM the night before last and forced into a black-plated car with the license plate number 6539, all aspects of the incident have been reported in this newspaper. Prominent Merchant Bei Run-sheng Entangled in Lawsuit

Accused of Instigating Embezzlement and Other Crimes

Has Been Bombed Four Times

Zhao Ke-qing, a deceased wealthy merchant from Suzhou, opened Qingfeng Yangbu Shop on Nanjing Road in the Guangxu year 15. Zhao Guan-qing, a relative, was appointed as manager. Later, Guan-qing also gathered funds to open Yisheng Yangbu Shop at the front of Qingfeng Shop, which was previously the most famous "Red Fence" among the foreign goods businesses. The shareholders were Bei Run-sheng and the now-deceased Zhao Yu-ting (a cousin of Zhao Ke-qing), among others. Guan-qing also had one share and served as the manager. In the Guangxu year 30, Yisheng Shop was reorganized and soon went bankrupt. Qingfeng Shop was also sealed by the former Mixed Court because it was in the same location. Manager Zhao Guan-qing, believing that shareholders Bei Run-sheng and Zhao Yu-ting's sons, Zhao Zhu-lin and his brothers, should be responsible for the debts under their shares, filed a lawsuit against Bei and Zhao Zhu-lin and his brothers in the former French Concession Court in the early years of the Republic of China, requesting that they be ordered to pay the outstanding debts they were responsible for. During the hearing, Bei denied being a shareholder of Yisheng, claiming he was merely an advisor. At the same time, Zhao Ke-qing's descendants, Zhao Jing-qing and his brothers, also claimed that Qingfeng Shop's funds had been misappropriated by Yisheng, resulting in the sealing of Qingfeng Shop, and they joined the lawsuit against Bei and others. The result was that they were all defeated. Guan-qing, dissatisfied with the original judgment, requested a retrial and appealed to the Third Branch of the Jiangsu Higher Court, but his appeal was rejected. Later, through the mediation of friends from both sides, Bei was ordered to pay Zhao Guan-qing 50,000 yuan to resolve the dispute. Now, Zhao Ke-qing's sons, Zhao Jing-qing, Zhao Zhuo-ru, Zhao Zu-zhang, and Zhao Yun-pu, claim that the profits from Qingfeng Shop, which was founded by their ancestors, had been misappropriated and embezzled by the shareholders of Yisheng Shop, Bei Run-sheng, Zhao Yu-ting, and others, with the instigation of manager Zhao Guan-qing, amounting to over 400,000 yuan. Because Yisheng went bankrupt and was sealed, Qingfeng was implicated, and the funds were lost. Zhao Guan-qing sued Bei Run-sheng and others, and Bei twice paid Guan-qing over 100,000 yuan (including the payment in the Republic of China year 17), which Zhao Yu-ting's sons, Zhao Zhu-lin and Dian-chen, handled. However, the funds misappropriated from Qingfeng Shop remained unrecovered, resulting in the loss of the shared property left by their ancestors. Therefore, they have hired three lawyers, Zhang Shi-zhao, Chen Ze-min, and Peng Yuan-xun, to file a private prosecution with the Second Special District Court, accusing Bei Run-sheng and Zhao Yu-ting's sons, Zhao Zhu-lin, Zhao Pin-hou, Zhao Yin-nian, and Zhao Guo-ping, and Zhao Guan-qing of instigating embezzlement and other crimes and requesting a legal investigation. (The lawsuit is lengthy and has been omitted.) The court issued summonses based on the complaint and scheduled a hearing for yesterday afternoon. The plaintiffs arrived at the court on time with their lawyers, Chen Ze-min. The defendant Bei Run-sheng (accompanied by his self-hired Russian bodyguard and four detectives assigned by the police for protection) and the Zhao brothers arrived at the court with their defense attorneys, Lu Shao-zong, Yu Zhong-luo, Peng Qi, and Jiang Bao-li. However, Zhao Guan-qing was represented by lawyer Li Mian due to illness. At the sound of the third bell, Judge Wu Fang-lian opened the Second Criminal Court for a special hearing. He summoned the parties and lawyers to the court. First, he asked each person's age, place of origin, address, and occupation. Then, Chen, the plaintiffs' attorney, began to state the purpose of the prosecution. Lawyer Li Mian then stated that he was representing the defendant Zhao Guan-qing because Zhao was ill and unable to get out of bed and had only been retained last night and had not yet studied the case. He requested that the court grant a postponement. The judge, considering that the key defendant Zhao Guan-qing was absent, adjourned the hearing. The defendant Bei Run-sheng then stated that although Zhao Guan-qing was absent today, the Zhao Zhu-lin brothers and others were present and could be interrogated. He also claimed that he had no shares in Yisheng and was merely an advisor. This case had been litigated by Zhao Guan-qing for a long time. Initially, Guan-qing negotiated with businessmen, and Zhou Wei-shi and Zhang Lan-ting mediated, ordering him to give Guan-qing 50,000 yuan. In the Republic of China year 20, Guan-qing was involved in litigation again, and the plaintiffs did not participate in the prosecution, resulting in a defeat. Later, Guan-qing requested a retrial, but it was still unsuccessful. The plaintiffs did not request a retrial. Later, Guan-qing appealed, and Du and Zhang mediated, and he paid 50,000 yuan. The case was closed. Now, the plaintiffs have suddenly filed a lawsuit, rehashing old matters, which is completely unreasonable and should be clearly recognized. The judge then questioned the plaintiff Zhao Jing-qing about the circumstances of the defendants' instigation of embezzlement and announced that a further hearing would be scheduled and instructed the plaintiffs that if the defendants filed a counterclaim, they should all appear at the next hearing. After finishing speaking, he adjourned the court. It is reported that Bei Run-sheng's house has been bombed four times this year, and now he is entangled in litigation again, which is truly unfortunate.

Reading Q&A

How to Train Our Brain (II)

｜｜Answer to Mr. Xu Lezhen

Before answering the several questions you have raised, we

cannot help but express our respect for you. It is very rare that you can so humbly and earnestly examine your past life. However, we also fully agree with your current "hope" ｜｜ "to develop an organized, rigorous, sensitive, and sound mind... to be a person who understands the times." ｜｜ But at the same time, we also have some supplementary opinions, which we will write out for your reference.

First, your "hope" seems a bit removed from practice, presented very abstractly. Of course, your desire to "be a person who understands the times" is very correct, but this conclusion is not derived from your life's struggles or bitter experiences. You only describe "environment" in a few dozen words in your entire letter. The entire letter is about your past reading life, and outside of reading, it seems you have quite neglected everything else. So your reading has become aimless, uncoordinated with real life, and it seems that you have not fully achieved application in every subject; and the categories are also very miscellaneous. Based on the letter, it can be seen that you are too isolated and indifferent to real life, completely trapped in the attitude of a so-called "pure scholar." You want to create yourself as a perfect person first, and then understand the times, or do something (you did not propose this point, but it is my speculation.) This is what we consider a big flaw.

Second, because you have the above concept, you think about "what subjects will make my brain rigorous, sound, sensitive, and eliminate unnecessary fantasies and delusions." This seems perfectly correct on the surface, but after realistic testing, it turns out that this is still a fantasy. Science does have the effect of training a person's brain to be sound, rigorous, and sensitive, but the soundness, rigor, and sensitivity of the brain can only be cultivated in social life, not by relying on science. Science suggests methods, brain training is in use. As for eliminating unnecessary "fantasies and delusions," it is not specifically dependent on reason. There are many theologians here who are also the most imaginative people. Breaking "fantasies and delusions" is only possible in real life, by replacing a loose and idle life with an organized and rational life. (To be continued)

Spring and Autumn

The Snow in Tiansi Village

— Yanqiao

"Leveling the rugged roads of the world, flying into the homes of the rich and noble." This is praising the fairness of snow, but the rugged roads, even if temporarily and superficially leveled, will soon reveal their true faces. And before the remaining snow melts, the ice becomes even more slippery and difficult to travel. As for the wealthy families, seeing the snow, they must prepare fine lamb and wine to appreciate it, without feeling the severity of winter at all. Then the so-called "fairness" is only this!

Tiansi Village is a special district of Suzhou, not in terms of administrative rights, but in terms of environment. After we walked through Wangxing Bridge and passed several small shops, we felt suddenly enlightened. The wintergreen trees in front of the John Hall and Boxi Hospital were like Christmas trees adorned with cotton, expressing their pure love. Looking at the white-robed nurses coming and going in the hospital, I wonder if those lying on the sickbeds know that the old sky has brought down heavy snow, and can they struggle to get up and look at the spectacle of city teeth biting the clouds and wild fields planting jade.

Several plane trees at Soochow University, originally as clear and sparse as old men, are now covered with snow, bloated and fat. The withered yellow of the grass has been completely replaced by pure white, and one does not feel the fear of the cold, but only the joy of the stillness. Although the young people are still active, fighting snow battles, most of them are hiding in the house after all. Climbing to the top floor, the "Twin Pagodas" stand side by side in the not-so-distant cluster of houses, as if children were stacking snow for fun. Everything has been added with poetic sentiment and artistic flavor, who has this great game except the old sky? Feeling that "it is not as good as willow catkins rising in the wind," is not getting rid of a girl's careful thoughts. "After the Jade Dragon has fought three hundred rounds, the remaining scales and armor fly all over the sky," is also too disproportionate to be considered heroic. On the other hand, Xiangling's "The towering jade tree has no shadow in the cold, and the fallen silver river does not flow when frozen," in A Dream of Red Mansions, is looking closely at the snow, is writing closely about the snow, especially today's Tiansi Village, which can be described and praised with these two lines of poetry. Because Tiansi Village has countless uneven trees, a vast ground, and a long road.

In Professor Ling's house, under the bright lights, sits an "old tune master" who came through the snow, pouting his flute to wait for Professor Ling to cheer up and sing his "official student" Kunqu Opera from his dantian, and with the flute sound drifting into the snow's enclosure. Then there is "rain silk and wind fragments, misty waves and painted boats." A girl's gentle throat. Ah! Not the evening prayer bell of the chapel, not the biolina and violin, not the song of "Dream Lover," this time of Tiansi Village is ours.

After the Snow

— Chen Liang

The old sky washed away its face full of lead gray, revealing a beautiful face.

A layer of snow piled up on the bridge railing, but it was as thin as frost. The bridge surface was a bit too slippery, people who are young and have good leg strength will not slip and fall, but for an old woman as old and weak as her, whose limbs have been frozen numb, it is really difficult.

An empty body is relatively better. However, she cannot lose the peanut basket on which she depends for life, and she has to hold a broken paper umbrella under her arm, tightly wrapping her own withered body in that thick, dirty, and tattered coat. She takes a step and breathes, and her small feet leave a very obvious triangle on the mud.

Carefully enough, she grabs the bridge railing with her left hand, letting the cold snowflakes stick to the palm of her hand, letting the wild wind blowing from the cold Huangpu River, stab into her skin like a sharp knife. Step by step, panting, she wants to get over this top bridge.

She herself never thought this way: "I'm old, I'm useless."

However, it is true that she is useless, "Ouch," she fell, the peanuts rolled away. Rolled away—the source of her life. Old people are weak, how can they withstand a fall? Once you fall, it is not easy to get up. There is no shortage of laughter around, but there are no arms to help her up. Want to find sympathy in this society? It's harder than finding anything else.

The old woman no longer waits for passers-by to help her, no longer waits for the mutual assistance that should exist between people. She struggles to get up, her hair white, her eyes white.

The basket is picked up, the broken paper umbrella is picked up, and the peanuts in the mud are also picked up.

On the bridge, she raises her thin head and looks at the fish-scale-like snow on the row of foreign roofs, blankly.

She feels that she is standing alone in this blank human world.

The Furnace is Burning

— Bo Guang

In the severe winter, we are naturally very happy to see the furnace burning. It is its heat that attracts people!

Shanghai's dance halls are all overcrowded. Dancers don't decrease due to the cold weather. The music is sonorous. The dancers embrace the dancing girls, dancing one melody after another. It is their heat that attracts people!

Shanghai brothels and private prostitutes in the mainland have an even better life on winter nights. Outside the window, the snow is white, inside the window, two feelings are intertwined. The two are as hot as fire, how can they know the cold outside the window? It is another kind of heat that attracts people!

Fourth Company Commander of the Northeast

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Twenty-Third: The Pain is Unbearable, He Listens Intently to the Music; The Joy is Not Exhausted, Farewell Arrives with a Flying Talisman

Ji Zhi was staring blankly when a messenger from his brother came out of the door. Without waiting for him to speak, he smiled: Look, isn't this a boring act? The messenger smiled: The second master will definitely hold his wedding at a restaurant in the city. Ji Zhi said: Me... Saying that, he smiled faintly and didn't say anything more. The messenger smiled: Look, people are also having a civilized wedding, military band and flower carriage, all here. When Ji Zhi looked forward, wasn't that right? A large group of military bands in red clothes, with big drums and brass flutes, were coming towards the Zhao family's door. At the same time, a flower carriage slowly drove and stopped at the Zhao family's door. Ji Zhi said: This is strange. The groom's family is in this gate, and the bride's family is also in this gate, what is the use of this flower carriage? When he said these words, his voice was a little high. A person near the tea stove walked up and smiled: The second master is short-sighted. The bride's family is borrowing our shop to hold the event. This place only counts as the groom's family. Later, they will send the flower carriage to our side to pick up the bride. Ji Zhi was called out by that person, and when he paid attention, he recognized him as a shop assistant from the milk tea shop. He smiled: You also do this line of business? The shop assistant smiled: Our boss used to do this line of business. There are few events held in the countryside, so he opened a milk tea shop on Haidian Street. Ji Zhi smiled: You are too good at doing business. You have taken on the groom's business, and you have also pulled the bride's family to your place. This way, the groom's family will have to spend more money on the flower carriage. The shop assistant smiled: You are saying the words backwards. People are doing it to show off the flower carriage, that's why the bride's family moved to our place. When I said this, I looked back at the people before whispering: Unexpectedly, the old Yang family's daughter is marrying this Company Commander Zhao. When Ji Zhi heard this, his heart moved, and he smiled at the shop assistant: Your words are a bit inconsistent. You feel that she shouldn't marry Company Commander Zhao, who should she marry then?

(299)

People on the Line of Struggle

— Yangtze River

The morning air is strangely cold. Although I am sitting in the corner of the wall basking in the sun, I actually don't get any warmth, because the sunlight is pitifully weak.

Peng, peng, peng, a small gong is ringing. One person is leading a monkey, and another person is carrying some of the monkey's things. They are knocking and walking in the alley, but not a single child comes out to watch the fun. The two monkey performers want to leave, but they stop again. They are patiently waiting, hoping for unexpected audiences and unexpected gains.

But it is cold, and it is morning. The children are hiding indoors. Although there is the enticement of the gong, they are still unwilling to go out. The monkey performers have no choice but to leave in disappointment, with lonely hearts and lonely sorrow.

For the sake of life, they have no choice but to brave the morning cold to move around, going east and west to attract young audiences. Undoubtedly, they are people on the line of bitter struggle.

Suddenly, here comes the mother and daughter who pick up garbage. The mother is a middle-aged woman over fifty years old, but the daughter is only a little girl of twelve or thirteen years old. The mother and daughter are quickly rummaging through the garbage can. Perhaps because it is early in the morning, the waste in the garbage can seems to be very rich. The mother is boldly opening the bottom door and hurriedly picking up what seems to be satisfactory. But unexpectedly, an old man who lives nearby walks up, loudly scolding them and driving them away.

The mother and daughter are still reluctant to leave, but the old man goes outside on his own. So, the daughter is patrolling, and the mother is still picking up garbage. But it seems that the fate of the poor is always bitter. The old man comes back from outside again. The mother receives the daughter's notification, and the mother and daughter hurriedly leave with their baskets. I am very upset, even the poor don't have the freedom to pick up garbage.

In my opinion, the mother and daughter also feel deeply saddened when they leave. The mother is so calm, and the daughter is so well-behaved. But for the sake of life, they cannot but endure the contempt of people and do that humble business. Undoubtedly, they are also people on the line of bitter struggle.

Movie Star Interview

— Yun Yan

I had wanted to meet Ms. Hu Die, the renowned figure in the movie industry, for a long time. However, despite several attempts, I hadn't been able to. The gatekeeper of the Star Film Company, an old Shandong man, was very courteous. Otherwise, for a down-on-my-luck person like me to visit such a beautiful woman of the times would truly be an intrusion upon Xi Shi [a legendary beauty]. Luckily, he was very kind and gave me a courteous reply. Yesterday, I was strolling aimlessly in the snow and ended up on Rue Dupleix. My feet knew it, and I found myself at the gate of the Star Film Company. I asked the old Shandong man again if Miss Hu had returned. This time I was truly fortunate. He said, "A car just went in. Go to the waiting room yourself, and someone will attend to you." I quickly went inside, announced my name, and asked for directions. Soon, a bright-eyed, white-toothed lady stood before me. Her face showed signs of travel, and it was clear she had just returned from a long journey and hadn't yet reapplied her makeup. I bowed and offered a few words of admiration, to which she responded with a gentle smile, revealing dimples from time to time. Later, I asked about her trip to Nanjing. She said, "I was very nervous. I am grateful for the support and applause of the audience in the capital, and I barely managed to avoid embarrassment. However, we took the night train back, and it was raining heavily and very cold in Nanjing. Many of us who went together caught colds. Some had runny noses, and some had chills and fever. I also have a headache and fear of the wind, so I just want to go back and rest..." And so, I took my leave.

Miscellaneous Reports

Let Me Also Talk About Goldfish

— Zheng Yimei

Mr. Wu Jiren sent me a book on goldfish breeding. After reading it, I became very interested and would like to talk about goldfish as well, to join the fun. Goldfish are a variant of the crucian carp, so they are also called gold crucian carp. Su Shunqin wrote in a poem: "Waiting for gold crucian carp by the bridge." In ancient times, keys were shaped like fish. Li Shangyin also had the line, "Firmly locking the osmanthus grove with golden fish locks." The other day, at the banquet of my old brother Jianwei at Yantang [Smoke Bridge], Zhuo Dai said, "Scatter silkworm eggs on new bricks and dry them in the hot sun, then throw them into the water, and they can turn into goldfish." But he only heard this from others and hasn't tried it himself. This year, he plans to try it in the pond of Lao Pu, and I don't know if it will succeed.

Among goldfish, there is a type called pearl scales, which is rarely seen in the world. The head is as red as a crane's crest, and the tail is as warm and moist as jade. The body is covered with small, protruding scales, each one round, as if wearing a pearl shirt. Mr. Fang Tiaochen of Dingyuan has a poem that says: "In my pond, clear and rippling, there are swimming fish, carefree. One fish has red scales, white on its ridge, another has speckled spots like hanging stars. Among them, one fish is truly outstanding, with small scales protruding, round like pearls, clearly revolving one by one, with silver threads running around its body. Its jade tail is long, reaching its shoulder, and it swims with a large belly, how convenient. Even more amazing, the fish's forehead is red and fresh, the color like coral, round like a coin (omitted below)." This poem can be included in a fish-raising manual. I wonder if this pearl scale species exists in the Fish Paradise?

In "Treatise on Superfluous Things," there are three sections on fish-watching water tanks, which should be adopted for raising goldfish: "Watching Fish: It is best to get up early, before sunrise. Whether in ponds or basins, fish all swim in clear springs and green pools. Also, on cool, clear nights with a moon, reflections are inverted in the waves, and from time to time, startled scales splash, awakening the eyes and ears. As for a gentle breeze rustling, making a harmonious sound, or after a rain, new water rises, with ripple patterns crinkling green, these are all good times to watch fish." Second, "Siphoning Water: Changing water in a basin every day or two will result in a greasy residue accumulating at the bottom. It is best to use a section of Xiang bamboo to make a siphon to remove it. If you don't siphon it out in time, the color will not be fresh and beautiful, so it is impossible to store it in a good fish pond." Third, "Water Tank: There are ancient bronze tanks, large enough to hold two dan [a unit of volume] of water, green all around. People in ancient times did not know what they were used for, but they must have been for pouring oil into to light lamps. Now, taking them to store fish is most ancient. Next, use porcelain from the Five-Colored Imperial Kiln, pure white ones are also acceptable. However, you must not use the flower pots fired in Yixing or the vulgar style of seven-dan cow legs. The reason I list this is really to prepare a kind of refined object to play with. If you must follow the diagram, it would also be conventional."

Li Huangpi has been gone for many years. I still remember that after he stepped down from the political stage, he lived in Tianjin, and gardens, flowers, trees, concubines, and sensual pleasures were his entertainment in his later years. A certain concubine, a Southerner, was inherently quiet. At flowery mornings and moonlit nights, she often lingered between the wind corridor and the water pavilion, so those who presented strange flowers and exotic plants from all directions were ordered by her to be planted by the gardeners, or they presented many goldfish, all top-quality dragon species, with protruding eyes and beautiful colors, and long fins and tails. The concubine loved to play with them, and a special Hao Pavilion was built to place the fish tanks. One day, the goldfish were suddenly caught and eaten by a lion-shaped cat. This cat was raised by Madam Wei, Huangpi's beloved concubine. The concubine did not know, and because she loved the goldfish, she crushed the cat to death. Madam Wei's maid ran to complain to her mistress. Madam Wei was furious and insisted that Huangpi deal with the concubine. However, the concubine argued that the cat had killed many goldfish, so it deserved to die. Each held their own views, and Huangpi repeatedly mediated, expending much effort. The concubine was ultimately a newcomer, and everyone sided with Madam Wei, saying: Eating fish is the nature of cats, and the concubine did not use other methods to stop it, but resorted to cruel means, which was unreasonable. The final solution was to kill all the goldfish in the tank to sacrifice to the cat. Although Madam Wei's anger subsided, the concubine was extremely angry and refused to eat. Huangpi secretly promised to buy her good fish again, and she barely managed to drink some porridge. A trusted actor said to Huangpi, "It is difficult for fish to be between two hates." He added, "It is difficult for a husband to be between two loves," which made Huangpi laugh.

Educational News From Other Regions

Chinese Educational Society Meeting Today

Meetings in the morning, reading papers and discussions in the afternoon.

｜Board of Directors meeting yesterday morning｜

(Nanjing, 24th) The Chinese Educational Society held a meeting of the Board of Directors on the morning of the 24th. Chairman Liu Tingfang presided. Regarding the research work progress plan of the society, it was decided (1) that the annual meeting would decide on specific topics and a committee would be formed to be responsible for carrying them out, and that branches would be asked to assist; (2) to introduce experimental research from various educational institutions; (3) to solicit independent research from individual members; (4) regarding the research topic plan for this year, it was decided that various proposed topics would be submitted to the general assembly for decision. It was decided to appoint Zhang Boling, Chen Jianxiu, Zhuang Zeding, Liu Tingfang, and Yang Lianggong as the presidium of the annual meeting, and Zheng Xigu was appointed to report on the society's affairs. As of the 24th, more than 30 people had registered at the Higher Education Institute of Central University. It is estimated that 80 to 90 members will attend this year's annual meeting. The opening ceremony will be held on the morning of the 25th.

Tong Runzhi, Pan Wen'an, and Sheng Langxi will read papers in the afternoon and discuss the working method of the society. On the morning of the second day, Chen Lijiang, Yang Lianggong, and Tao Zhihang will read papers and discuss educational issues. In the afternoon, there will be discussions of the society's affairs and elections. (Nanjing, 24th) Zhang Boling is scheduled to arrive in Beijing on the morning of the 25th to attend the meeting. The Beijing Municipal Primary and Secondary School Social Education Institutions and the Beijing Branch are scheduled to hold a public banquet for all members at the Central Hotel at noon on the 25th.

Results of Junior High School Graduation Exam in Zhejiang Province Announced

408 students were approved to graduate.

206 students were approved to take make-up exams or repeat grades.

The Education Department of Zhejiang Province held the graduation examination for secondary school students in the first semester of the 22nd academic year on January 9th and 10th, simultaneously in three districts. As reported in this newspaper, 614 junior high school graduates took the examination this time, along with 189 students who failed one or two subjects in the first and second semesters of the 21st academic year and students who failed three or more subjects and were repeating the grade. This time, they were all allowed to participate in this year's examination, for a total of 803 people. It is now known that the examination papers have been graded. Apart from the re-examination and repeater students being announced separately, the grades of this year's junior high school graduates in the first semester were all passing. Those who were approved to graduate include 57 students in Grade A, such as Tan Shaozeng, 283 students in Grade B, such as Xu Changti, and 68 students in Grade C, such as Zhu Xirang. 172 students failed one or two subjects and were allowed to participate in the next examination for those subjects. 34 students failed three or more subjects and should repeat the grade. It is said that the above announcement will be posted at the gate of the Education Department today (the 25th).
