Free Talk

Random Talk on Ritual and Doctrine

— Feng Zi

After Emperor Gaozu of Han ascended to the throne, because the ministers were unrestrained, he felt that the taste of sitting on the dragon court was not necessarily better than living in a cool pavilion. It was not until Sun Tong had established the court etiquette that he suddenly realized the nobility of being the Yellow Emperor and felt the need for ritual and doctrine.

In fact, those who need ritual and doctrine are only emperors. Those who advocate ritual and doctrine often only think for emperors and kings. They often put shackles on the masses, separating people with high walls, and only giving a few careerists special privileges. If someone gets rid of the shackles, climbs over the high walls, and even shakes the special privileges of the careerists, that is betraying ritual and doctrine, becoming a "rebellious minister and traitor," and "everyone can punish him."

However, this is not an immutable law.

If the "rebellious minister and traitor" can become an emperor, the gentlemen who advocate ritual and doctrine will immediately come with the signboard of ritual and doctrine. This time, naturally, they are still thinking for the emperor and king. Once the rebellious minister and traitor sits on the dragon court, he will inevitably have ambitions. Since the shackles cannot lock himself, and there are still many benefits, he might as well do a favor. Therefore, for thousands of years, the various schools of thought were dismissed as heresies and almost completely lost, but Confucius was able to stand tall alone.

Confucius's towering presence is also the reason why ritual and doctrine do not fall behind. Moreover, scholars also want to use it as their housekeeping skills and promote it vigorously. Thus, men subjugate women, which is ritual; masters oppress servants, which is ritual; superiors drive subordinates, which is ritual; and as for emperors governing the country, it is of course indispensable to ritual and doctrine. This understanding becomes deeper and deeper, and it reaches the point where even if one is not a "rebellious minister and traitor," but "if the ruler wants the minister to die," then the minister "must die."

This is where "perhaps" arises.

But the more tragic result is the scene of defending Suiyang City to the death. According to the Tang History, Biography of Loyalty and Righteousness: "Zhang Xun defended Suiyang City, and the siege by the rebels lasted for a long time. The food in the city was exhausted, and children were exchanged for food, and bones were broken for firewood. Xun then took out his concubine, killed her in front of the three armies, and feasted the soldiers, saying, 'Please, gentlemen, work hard for the country to defend the city, with one heart and no second. Xun cannot cut his own flesh to feed the soldiers, so how can he regret this woman!' The soldiers all shed tears and could not bear to eat her. Xun forcibly ordered them to eat her. After the women in the city were exhausted, they were followed by men, old and young, and the population eaten was twenty to thirty thousand."

This time, it reached the point where the husband had to kill his wife, and the official had to kill the people, and they all had to die. Because to preserve one's loyalty to the master and complete the ritual and doctrine, one does not hesitate to sacrifice the innocent. What is so-called ritual and doctrine, in this case, reveals its true face: it turns out to be a man-eating demon!

In Defense of "Critics"

— Ye Rong

"Critics" seem to have become the target of public criticism recently. If they point out shortcomings, they are guilty of "devastation," and it is said that they "killed the wrong person." However, if they praise a work, they are guilty of "nervousness," making the literary world "filled with joy," which does not help the development of culture. The former has already been regarded as a "thug," and it is said that the "suffocated writers" will be kicked into the "cold palace" and suffer some confinement. The latter also has many people who are verbally criticizing and writing against them.

This reaction comes partly from the "group of writers," who say that their creation is suffocated by "criticism." On the other hand, it does not seem to be writers, but some chivalrous people who are speaking out for the writers. Judging from their tone of compassion for the future of culture and the writers, it can be seen that they are third parties standing by.

Critics, caught in the crossfire, seem to be speechless, knowing that their sins are heavy and have no excuse to answer. However, the person who jumped onto the stage and chopped the actor playing Cao Cao to death with an axe is actually not a critic today, but the real Cao Cao who is being played. Although the woodcutter is also in the audience today, he is not so confused that he cannot tell black from white, or distinguish between truth and falsehood. Moreover, the position of a critic is not the same as the position of a woodcutter in the audience, and besides, it is the real Cao Cao who wants to chop him with an axe?

If he "killed the wrong person," it was only out of "misunderstanding," not because he had a feud with the actor, which is excusable.

What a true critic wants to point out is whether Cao Cao's social existence is real, and how well the actor plays and sings Cao Cao. If Cao Cao is played as Yue Fei, or Yue Fei is played as Cao Cao, then chopping him with an axe is justified. The direction of the critic's axe is in this direction, not on the stage, and even less on the actor on the stage.

Critics are not afraid of Cao Cao being played vividly, but hate that the actors cannot vividly present Cao Cao to the audience. They hate that the ones playing Cao Cao are the Cao Caos themselves, and the ones who want to chop the actors to death are also Cao Cao. Because he plays too much like themselves. The actors should not "mistake the enemy." Although I am not a critic, I am speaking out for the true critics. Critics will not "kill the wrong person." If there is a "misunderstanding," it is the responsibility of the individual who executes the "axe punishment." Therefore, the "woodcutter" is always a woodcutter, not a critic.

Insomnia

— Zhou Fenjia

For the past few days, I have been suffering from insomnia almost every night.

Insomnia is not a serious symptom, but it is a threat to people who lead a life of mental labor. I don't know how this insomnia started. As usual, I go to bed at ten o'clock every night. The bed has a light switch, and as long as I reach out and turn off the light, I can fall into a dream. In dreams, all human beings are equal, whether they are rich people with millions of dollars or small people with no way out.

However, one night, the situation was different. I turned off the light as usual, gave a last glance at the darkness surrounding me, and closed my eyelids, ready to go to the land of sweet dreams to find my good dreams. Unexpectedly, although my eyelids were closed, dreams kept me out of the door, as if everything was destined for me to suffer a night of torment. I tossed and turned, unable to fall asleep. My mind was like a special express train, and my thoughts were surging endlessly without stopping.

The first thing that entered my mind was the issue of the "Beijing School" and "Shanghai School" in the literary world. Then, the eight characters "Celebrities, talent, commercial competition, auction" quickly flashed through my mind. Next, from the "Beijing School" and "Shanghai School" in the literary world, I thought of the "Beijing School" and "Shanghai School" in the theater world, and thought of Mei Lanfang's "Drunken Concubine" and Xiao Dazi's "The Civet Cat for the Prince." I thought that the drama performed by the rough and strange Xiao Dazi was certainly not as good as the drama performed by Dr. of Literature Mei Lanfang, and that the "Shanghai School" was certainly not as good as the "Beijing School." Finally, I felt that the word "Beijing School" was a bit inappropriate and should be changed to "Beiping School" Because Beijing has now been renamed Beiping, and Beijing opera has also been renamed Ping opera. If people in the literary world still call themselves the "Beijing School," they will inevitably be seen as having some suspicion. Thinking this way, thoughts emerged one after another, and the dreamland moved further and further away from me.

Suddenly opening my eyes, what appeared before me was a mass of darkness. This darkness made me distressed, and I couldn't help but think that there were many things to do tomorrow, and I must fall asleep tonight, otherwise, even if I could barely do things tomorrow, I would be extraordinarily tired, and all the planned plans would be finished. Therefore, I tried to force those thoughts and force myself into the dreamland.

"Sleep! One, two, three, four, five, six, seven, eight..." I silently recited the numbers. This was taught to me by a friend, who said that it had unexpected power. People with insomnia only need to keep reciting, and before they reach a hundred, they will unknowingly fall into a dream. Now, I tried it out. But when I was still awake after counting nearly a thousand, I knew that this method was not working and I had to find another way. Another way was to put my hand under my left breast and try to think about my feet, so that the blood in my head would flow down and it would be easier to fall asleep. This was what I read in a book. It was not difficult to put it into practice. It was just that thinking about my feet was too boring. It would be better to think about my buttocks, which would probably also allow the blood in my head to flow down. So, I tried my best to concentrate my thoughts on my buttocks. Who knew that this would be even worse! My thoughts quickly turned from my buttocks to Mr. Lin Yutang's article "On Kicking Butts," and from that article to the joke mentioned in the Ku Cha An Jokes Collection that ridiculed comparing heads to buttocks, and sleep was even more difficult to come to me.

The sky brightened while I was trying to sleep. The sky was bright, and I had to get up and do things. As soon as I did things, I was terribly tired and yawning constantly, and I just wanted to lie down on the bed and sleep. With great difficulty, I managed to get to bed, and as soon as my head hit the pillow, I couldn't fall asleep again. Everything was just a continuation of last night. Thoughts were still surging, my mind was still running on a special express train, and there was even more of a sound:

"Run faster! America, run faster!"

This was the name of a short story, and the author was forgotten, probably the American Gold. I don't know why, but at this time, it kept echoing in my mind continuously. In order to make this sound disappear, I had to replace it with another kind of thought. So, I thought of Puyi becoming emperor, the feeling of sitting on the throne, Qin Shihuang, Alexander, Napoleon, Wilhelm II, Hitler, and World War II. At this time, my mind made a "boom" sound, as if the gunpowder depot of the Second World War had exploded.

In this way, I watched another night of darkness with my eyes wide open. Several nights in a row passed in insomnia. Fatigue, disappointment, and distress attacked my weak body, and I really couldn't hold on any longer. I repeatedly wanted to go to the pharmacy to buy a bottle of sedative water to drink, but I was always stopped by my wife. My wife's cowardly heart was always afraid that if I drank sedative water, I would fall into a long sleep and never wake up. But she didn't know that I was eager to be able to sleep forever. Because once I slept forever, I wouldn't have to face the darkness every night, I wouldn't have to fear the arrival of World War II, and I wouldn't have to fear bowing to Puyi, who was about my age one day.

Review of "Jealousy"

— Shi Heng

Recently, the Commercial Press published a play titled "Jealousy," translated by Mr. Li Liewen during his time in France.

Regarding the French playwright J.J. Bernard, I have no prior knowledge. However, based solely on his play "Jealousy," we can discern that he is an exceptionally talented playwright.

"Jealousy" was originally titled "Le Feu qui reprend mal" (The Fire That Rekindles Poorly). The translator, deeming the original title cumbersome, renamed it "Jealousy." However, I believe the original title better expresses the play's meaning, as we cannot merely regard this book as "a new page in the study of jealousy" (in the words of the critic Regis Gignour). Whether intentional or not, the author presents more profound issues within this play, issues related to the previous World War.

The plot is remarkably simple, with only four characters: a married couple, the wife's elderly father, and a female friend. The setting is a small city in France, taking place after the European war. The husband, Andre, is a high school teacher who was captured at the beginning of the war and imprisoned in the Darmstadt camp for four years. During this time, his wife, Blanche, endured four years of anticipation and suffering. However, in the last few months, like many households in that small city, she housed an American soldier. Later, she explained this to her friend, Jeanne: "The Mayor insisted so earnestly. You can believe that I would never have wanted to otherwise. But the Mayor told me that in a small town like ours, a teacher's wife should set a good example. Andre would have told me the same thing if he were here. That is why I accepted." However, on the very day the armistice was signed, when the father, wife, and friends enthusiastically welcomed Andre home, he became suspicious and jealous of his wife. Subsequently, almost without any concrete evidence, the play portrays the development of the husband's doubts and jealousy. The happiness of the reunited couple, which he had dreamed of for four years, never materializes, and they argue every day. This harsh reality brings Blanche a disappointment that surpasses all the pain she had endured for four years:

Blanche (pensively)... Andre was captured. At that time, I had a duty. He was not by my side; he was unfortunate, so he could compete. But now he has returned, and he is not the same Andre.

Jeanne, you take your own disappointment too seriously; you are not as forgiving as you used to be.

Blanche Perhaps so; but everyday life is so ruthless! It shows us all the worst aspects of the people we love... Since he returned, Andre is just an ordinary man in my eyes.

It is this ruthless everyday life that forces her to leave her husband and follow the American soldier, who lived in the same house as her for several months, to a new world. Although nothing ever happened between them, he expressed his love for her when he left, and they still correspond. Although she does not actually leave, and although at the end of the play, she says to her suspicious and jealous husband, "Oh, how can you ask me to leave?" her heart is broken. She is experiencing profound disillusionment, and her future life is destined to be unhappy. (To be continued)

Father and Daughter (6)

— Jin Yi

She seemed to fully understand the suffering in her father's heart, knowing that this was a natural path for him to take given his circumstances. Her resentment towards her father had subsided, and condemnation had turned into comfort.

"From now on, child, I promise you from the bottom of my heart—I will never bring a drop of alcohol near my lips again!" He made the greatest resolution, his eyes wide as he spoke.

"I know you will do it, for your daughter, for yourself."

After she said that, she lifted her face and leaned close to his.

It was already broad daylight, and the beautiful autumn morning light streamed in through the gaps in the curtains, shining on them. She helped her father up, slowly stood up, walked to the window, pulled back the curtains, and looked at the scenery outside. Before her were piles of blood-red maple leaves, so vibrant, that it was hard to believe that in a few days they would fall to the ground and be trampled into dust. The road was already covered with yellow fallen leaves, which had also had good days as green as jade; but autumn had ended everything, and they could only lie peacefully on the ground.

He stared intently, as if deep in thought, and then nodded slightly, muttering:

"I must cherish myself, I must cherish myself!"

The daughter, standing by his side, smiled at him when she heard these words, the sunlight shining on their faces with an unusual radiance. After that, they lived even more peacefully, passing through autumn and into the bleak winter days. But their hearts were warm, father and daughter giving each other comfort.

One evening, the father went to the bachelor's club, because there was a lecture by a well-known person there. She was sitting alone in the sitting room, knitting a wool coat for her father. A snow-white Persian cat, sent by a friend, was playing with the ball of yarn. She watched it with interest, but her hands did not stop working. At this moment, the maid came in and said to her:

"Miss, there is a female guest outside to see the master."

"What, a female guest?"

She put down her work, asking with a hint of surprise.

"Yes, she looks like she's in her thirties, she came alone in a car."

"Didn't you tell her that the master is not at home?"

"She said she would like to see the young lady as well."

"She knows me?"

"It seems she does."

"Then please, show her in."

She stood up, brushed the loose wool from her clothes, and ran her fingers through her hair; a great doubt arose in her heart. For so many years, there had never been a single female guest visiting her father, what kind of woman could this be? The female guest had already walked in with the maid, and suddenly it was as if a weak current ran through her body. She doubted her eyes, widened them a little more, and her heart began to tremble. She wanted to call out something, but she immediately knew that it was too inappropriate, so she forced herself to hold back. She saw that the woman was also staring at her, blankly, as if she had forgotten herself. She saw that the woman was nearly fifty years old, but had a good figure, fashionable clothes, and with her special makeup, looked easily ten or fifteen years younger. At the corner of her eye, she clearly saw that red mole. The female guest also seemed to want to suddenly shout something, but she swallowed it back, and only stammered:

This Month's Cotton Shows Signs of a Short Squeeze

The cotton market is firm again, with the delivery period for this month approaching, and sellers lacking sufficient chips to clear their positions. Short sentiment is increasingly strong, showing signs of a short squeeze. Distant months have also been stimulated, but spot cotton transactions are particularly scarce. According to some, there are hundreds of thousands of dans of cotton stored in Hankou, but due to excessive moisture, it is difficult to export to Shanghai.

Zheng Standard Slightly Smart: At the opening of the Zheng standard market, scattering short covering for this month caused prices to rise across the board by 2.1-3 cents. In the afternoon, large long players closed their positions, causing prices to fall by 0.05-0.15 cents. The total transaction volume for the day was 71,400 dans. It was found that Yuanda sold 8,200 dans, Shenchang 2,300 dans, Tongfu 1,000 dans, Tongji 1,500 dans, Yongchang 1,200 dans, Xinheng 2,200 dans, Chuangji 2,000 dans, Tonghe 1,700 dans, Changhe 1,700 dans, and Jifeng 1,700 dans. Dafeng bought 4,300 dans, Changfeng 6,800 dans, Gengfeng 1,600 dans, Renfeng 1,700 dans, Hengyi 2,100 dans, Xiesheng 2,100 dans, and Yuchang 1,600 dans. Closing prices are as follows:

Slight Rise in US Cotton Futures

Yesterday, US cotton initially fell due to mass selling, but later rose due to spot merchants buying and strength from Wall Street. As a result, the spot price remained unchanged, while futures rose by two to four points. Liverpool cotton spot prices fell by one point, and futures fell by ten to eleven points. Egyptian cotton spot prices fell by thirteen points. The Bombay cotton market initially fell due to long positions closing, but later rebounded as brokers bought on behalf of Japanese merchants. As a result, Pingar rose by 2.5 angles, Ormla fell by 1.5 rupees, and Bai Luo Creek fell by 7.5 angles. (Original telegraph from the 23rd)

Food Factories Massively Sell Futures Flour, Prices Fall Back

After the flour market opened yesterday morning, the market for each month generally showed a tired and falling trend. Although the quotation for foreign wheat improved by 0.20 outside of Chicago, and even more in Canada, people inside and outside the industry were not encouraged by this. It was rumored in the market that the government was borrowing wheat and there were two more ships for sale, with the price being 4.20 yuan, delivered in Shanghai, to be purchased proportionally by large and small factories. Therefore, market sentiment was already weak, and factory selling was also strong, with the market showing declines across the board. When the market opened in the afternoon, factories continued to sell distant months, but because buying interest was weak, the volume of selling was not high. As for the current month, because of mutual competition between longs and shorts, the changes were negligible. As a result, the current month was slightly down by 0.005 yuan compared to the previous day, February fell by 0.0225 yuan, March and April fell by 0.0175 yuan, May fell by 0.015 yuan, and June fell by 0.0125 yuan.

Distant New Wheat Breaks Eight-Angle Threshold

Yesterday's futures wheat market generally showed a flat and tired trend. Although the quotation for foreign wheat improved by 0.10 and 0.20 yuan, the current month, due to the approaching settlement, longs were eager to sell back. Factories were importing foreign wheat, and it seemed they had no intention to accept delivery. Therefore, it finally fell to as low as 3.95 yuan, down another 0.03 yuan from the previous day. Distant trading remained not very active, with limited fluctuations. However, June had already broken the 0.80-angle threshold, falling to 0.79 angles. It is said that if the government were to sell wheat together, there would be little hope for standard wheat.

客秈 (Ke Xian) Only Has 福州 (Fuzhou) as a Route

||Prices Continue to Rise by 0.05 or 0.06 yuan||

Yesterday, Ke Xian rice from Minhua was very active. Since the end of the war, the Fuzhou gang has had a very strong demand from various places. In recent days, Chinese merchant ships have been opening up daily, so the Fuzhou gang is quite enthusiastic. In addition to the Fuzhou provincial gang, the Xiamen, Quanzhou, and Xinghua gangs also have businesses. However, because everything has not yet been properly coordinated, only a small number of Hakka people are contacting merchants to arrange for loading. The market has not yet opened up, and the spot goods have not yet been loaded. The appetite of the provincial gang continues to increase. Yesterday, more than 1,000 bags were traded, and the price has risen by 0.05 or 0.06 yuan. Brokers are still optimistic and are quoting prices 0.10 yuan higher, so the gang has not been able to conduct business smoothly. Our street and the Zhejiang gang also have an appetite, but because the price is rising, they dare not do too much. Yesterday, our street traded more than 1,000 bags, and the Zhejiang gang did not move. According to the current activity of this Ke Xian rice, the market still needs to be optimistic. However, the inventory in the market is very sufficient, and deliveries arrive daily, so prices have not yet jumped.

Suzhou Tong Geng Price Good, Up 0.05 Yuan

(Hu Nan) Yesterday, the sources for all gangs were scarce, with only ship numbers 25 and 26 arriving (totaling over 3,000 shi). The wholesale and retail appetite from our street was relatively lackluster, so the price of Chang gang, Suzhou Tong gang's thick Geng rice increased by 0.05 yuan. However, South Port's early rice did not show any change. As for late rice, the customer's interest in bagged rice has turned lazy, so the whole city only took 500-600 bags of Si Song high-quality goods from the Beiyang gang. Therefore, most late rice such as Qing Jiao and Xi Lian were only moving in small quantities. Fortunately, the market did not have much arriving goods and still appears steady. Du Yang's top-quality goods lacked flavor, and the market showed a brisk color. Yin Yuan seems to be slightly stable, while Bian Yuan is still outstanding.

(Hu Bei) Yesterday, 50 or more ships arrived from various routes along the river. The inland river freezing has cleared, and the sales appetite for various colors in the market has slightly moved. The market for white Geng, Yang Du, Bu Ke, and top-quality goods is stable. White Yuan has tightened by several points. Early thin rice Yin Yuan is firm. The bagged goods are carefully being moved.

Green Beans are Plentiful, Market is Tired

The market condition for green beans has been flat for a long time. There are not many sources. The bottom inventory is about 50,000 to 60,000 bags of both Ming and Mao green beans. However, Ming green beans are more numerous than Mao green beans. The main outlet is Nanhua, and the Beiyang has the Yantai gang. Western merchants are not as continuous in their trading as in previous years, so it is not easy for the market to improve. However, the selling price of high-quality vegetable green beans is 5.12 yuan, which is probably the bottom. Yesterday, the market had a Western firm, Gao Zeng Foreign Firm, purchasing 799 bags of high-quality vegetable green beans, with the price being 5.18 yuan, which is said to be an unprocessed price.

Sugar Market Gradually Turns Upwards

||Chao Qing Returns Soft||

Yesterday, the sugar market continued to rise due to the rise in Customs Gold and the shrinking of the Dutch exchange rate, making the trend even tighter. The association’s marked price for No. 24 coarse granulated white common goods was 19.60 yuan, up 0.20 yuan from the previous day. Transit goods were quoted up by 0.15 yuan, at 6.70 yuan. Old Dutch red goods were 16 yuan, and new goods were 15.75 yuan. Taikoo Sugar B mark was quoted up to 20 yuan, but the deal did not go through. The factory's refined white sugar was in short supply, and Zhenyu No. 1 also rose by 0.20 yuan to 18.80 yuan. Changxing opened more than 1,000 bags of Zheng refined Dutch white sugar, with the price being 19 yuan. Chao Qing did not continue to open because the opinions of the firms on both sides did not come close, and the market trend looked small.

North-South Goods Bitter Apricot Kernels Scarce and Surprisingly Popular

Bitter apricot kernels are now in short supply because there is no continuing supply, and the inventory is thin. At the same time, there is demand from the sales side, making the trend tight and popular. Yesterday, the higher-priced goods in the market were being asked for over 30 yuan by customers, up about 10 yuan from the lowest price.

An Overview of the Daily Necessities Market (4) Xi Nan

Originally, in our country, the shopkeepers provided food and lodging for their employees, and the salaries they received were only for supporting their families. Since the "foreign firm system" became popular, this food and lodging issue has changed. It is included in the salary and is no longer provided. Later, our country's banks and companies also did the same. Therefore, friends who work in companies and firms have a problem with eating. Besides going home to eat, they have to go to restaurants, but both are expensive. Frugal friends then sometimes eat dry food, and sometimes order food temporarily. Especially in the area from East Sichuan Road to the Bund, where foreign firms, banks, large companies, and customs are located, the resolution of the eating problem for general staff is very serious. However, in this world, if there is a need, there will be a supply. Temporary canteens established for consumption are also like bamboo shoots after a rain. The most famous is the road next to the Bank of Communications, where there are actually signs saying "Food Available on the Left," with braised beef, coffee, bread, toast, etc., available. On Sundays, it also rests like other firms. North of the Waibaidu Bridge, in the Hongkou and Yangshupu areas, there are many docks, so there are only things like fried dough sticks and large pancakes, just to fill the stomachs of coolies.

Along the river, regarding food, there is also the fish market in the French Concession's 16 Pu. Their transactions are fair. When most people are still soundly asleep, before dawn, the peddlers who rush to the small vegetable market take advantage of this time to transport goods to sell on various roads. Therefore, fishmongers are also gathered here, and 青蘿乾 (preserved radish) and 紫大頭 (purple mustard tuber) are their related businesses.

16 Pu is also the "birthplace" of fruit shops. There are many fruit shops along Dongmen Road 裏馬路 (Inner Horse Road). However, some people say that bananas and sugar cane produced in South Guangdong are found in places like Wusong Road. Buying fruit is indeed cheaper to buy from shops, but that is not always the case. If you know how to buy, you can buy cheaper goods from peddlers. Especially the scales of the shops are so small that it is inexplicable. Approximately, what they call a catty is less than a pound. This situation is not only unavoidable for fruit shops, but even large domestic goods stores claim that ten catties of oranges cost one yuan, but when re-weighed, it is only about eighty taels, which is even more unbelievably "small." (To be continued)

Silk and Tea Silk Market Becomes More Depressed

(Yongheng Silk Factory Announces Shutdown Again) The local silk factory industry has not seen any improvement in overseas silk sales. Only one or two Bao Tai Shun factories in Nanshi and five single and double yarn silk factories such as 　Cang in Zhabei and Yongheng Fu Hui in Hongkou barely resumed work during the New Year. Unexpectedly, the European and American silk markets continued to be sluggish, with no actual sales. Domestic 　gate sales were sluggish and suffered losses, so it was difficult for the factories to sustain themselves. Yongheng Silk Factory (208 silk machines) on Tianbao Road, Hongkou, announced its shutdown again the day before yesterday. Currently, it is estimated that only four silk factories are operating in the city, including Bao Tai Shun. Among them, Heng Cang and other two factories are still reeling silk for customers with the remaining cocoons. As soon as they are used up, they will have to stop working.

(Yellow and White Silk Waste Exports Decrease Further) Yellow and white silk waste exports are increasingly deteriorating. Exports decreased further last week. Only 537 dan were loaded onto various postal ships to Europe and the United States, of which only 1 dan was loaded to Indian territories.

(European and American Silk Sales Are Unlikely to Improve) The Yokohama Japanese silk market saw uncertain fluctuations in current silk prices. New York standard silk prices remained hovering. Lyon and London prices showed no change. Various silk factories had sufficient silk inventory to meet demand. Telegrams relayed to Shanghai were scarce. Hua 　merchants had difficulty selling silk in their hands at low prices. Market sentiment was pessimistic. Silk sales are unlikely to improve in the short term. Yesterday, only inland silk factories purchased 40 bales of white factory silk. Repayment remained firm.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Commentary

Things Gentlemen Do

— Yunfei

The National Goods Exhibition organized by Shanghai grandmothers, wives, and young ladies has an exhibition room called "Model Family." The so-called model family is a magnificent living room and bedroom combined. Looking at the price tags of all the furniture in that room, it costs 1,000 yuan.

Indeed, there are many things these days that are ostensibly designed for the public good, but in reality, they are just things gentlemen do. For example, the above-mentioned case. Its name is the National Goods Exhibition, and its promotional target is the "Model Family." According to common sense, these "national goods" should be national goods that everyone can use, and this model family should at least be a "family" that everyone can "model." However, in fact, the so-called model family requires "furniture worth 1,000 yuan" - things in the world are often so comical. The name may sound good, but the reality is just a set of deceptive tricks.

There are really many such things in society. For example, when it comes to hygiene, a group of people always tells others to have proper nutrition, drink a glass of milk every morning, exercise more, avoid overworking, and go for a walk in the park on Sundays so that their bodies will become stronger. If they get sick, they should see a doctor immediately and never listen to the nonsense of witches and Taoists, offering sacrifices to ghosts and eating elixirs, as this will lead to death. These words sound reasonable enough. But in reality, they can barely afford to eat two large pancakes a day, and it is already difficult to eat some white rice and vegetables, let alone anything like milk. As for work, it is like that of oxen and horses. Exercise and rest are completely out of the question for them. When they get sick, doctors - whether Western or Chinese - are out of reach. Who else can they turn to but witches and Taoists? The reward they require is, in any case, only a few cents or a few hundred cash, which is truly in line with their means. And as for education, people often clamor for universal education, to enable children in rural areas to read. Therefore, they try their best to promote schools in rural areas, and are afraid that farmers will not be able to afford their children's tuition fees and will not send them to school. Therefore, there are also occasionally a few free primary schools set up, with all tuition fees and books provided by the school. Students only need to spend some time studying. This can be considered the utmost benevolence and righteousness towards farmers, and universal education is no longer a problem. But in reality, there are still a large number of farmers who are unwilling to let even one child attend free school. Because they need a child to do the work of one person. When the fields are busy, they need children to help. When they are free, they also need children to gather firewood or herd cattle, which is equivalent to half a worker's work. Asking their children to study is tantamount to taking away half a worker from them. They know the benefits of literacy, but they would rather have their children illiterate than lose half a worker for nothing. As a result, free schools are free schools, farmers are still farmers, and the problem of universal education is still not solved. Other social issues are similar to this everywhere. People always only think from the top, and are unwilling to think from the bottom, so the result is always in vain. In fact, what society needs most at present is not good words like hygiene and education, but the most basic and minimal "eating" problem. Only when the eating problem is solved can we talk about other things. At present, they don't even have food to eat. Where do they have the mood to think about things other than eating? However, how can we make them have food to eat? The general upper class in society does not think about this. They only know how to stand on high ground and sing high-sounding tunes, saying cool words.

I remember that there was a great famine in France many years ago, and many people starved to death. The French princess said that it was easy to relieve the famine, so how could people starve to death? Although this is a folk legend and may not be reliable, it also shows that the rich do not know the suffering of the poor. The gap between them is truly beyond expectation. Most of the social undertakings that the ladies and gentlemen are pursuing at present are also like the cold sickness that Lü Mengzheng pointed out.

A certain important person once said such a sentence. He said that it is wrong for us to learn from the United States now. The United States is a rich country, and we are a poor country. We can only do things the poor way. If we learn from the United States, the result will be that nothing will be done well. These few words are very meaningful. I also want to quote his words now, what we need to solve most urgently now is the problem of everyone having food to eat, not the social undertakings in the mouths of you adults and gentlemen - if you really want to run social undertakings, then please start from this aspect first. We don't need the games that gentlemen play at all now.

The Three Lines of Literati

— Mei

"A good article is good in itself" is the most common saying among Chinese people. This saying fully reveals the self-pride and arrogance of Chinese literati. Originally, China has vast land, magnificent mountains and rivers, and at the same time, among the 400 million people, those who are literate - this refers to non-illiterate, not literati - according to last year's statistics, only account for 10%. From this point of view, the self-pride and arrogance of literati is actually promoted by the natural and social environment, and it is not the fault of the literati themselves.

The self-pride and arrogance of literati is not necessarily based on their "one word is worth a thousand gold" mentality. If literati should be self-proud and arrogant just because they know how to write a few words, then why do the literary beggars in Shanghai and Nanjing kneel on the roadside and write long self-descriptions with chalk for the appreciation of many "passing gentlemen," but the price they get is only dozens of copper coins, which is not enough to fill their stomachs? From this, we can know that the self-pride and arrogance of literati has other reasons.

Page 20

The self-pride and arrogance of literati lies in three lines. What are the three lines? They are "I'm good, you're not good, and he's not good either." Here, "good" does not mean the meaning of walking, but is a hidden word for "good." The so-called "I'm good, you're not good, and he's not good either" seems to mean "My work is good, yours is not good, and his is not good either," or "I can write good articles, you can't, and he can't either." When I was young, I studied and was also listed among the literati. I often hung out with literati. When literati saw the books displayed on my bookshelf, they suddenly pointed to a certain book and said "not good," and then pointed to another book and said "also not good." In their words, it seemed that only they themselves were "good." Are today's critics any different? In their writing, none of other people's articles are "good." In their words, it seems that only their own articles are "good." A literati all hold the "I'm good" ideology in the three lines, so Chinese literati all "become good"! All literati have studied rhetoric, so their sentence-making can be just right. Although literati hold the "I'm good" ideology, they never announce "I'm good" to the public. What they announce to the public is "you're not good" or "he's not good either," because "you're not good" and "he's not good either" are equal to "I'm good." This is like A squared times B squared equals C squared in algebra. But once a certain literati with the "I'm good" ideology is fortunately valued, then we "not good" literati all eagerly hope for the appearance of a great work by that certain literati. Unexpectedly, the great work of that certain literati is again listed as "not good" in the writing of many critics, so another certain literati with the "I'm good" ideology rises up to succeed him. They fall and stand in turn, and as a result, everyone is a "genius," and everyone is a "feeble-minded child." So far, we have not found a real "I'm good" writer in these three lines.

This is the great transformation of the Chinese literary world in recent years, and it is also the strange phenomenon of the Chinese literary world in recent years.

Waiting

— Zu

It snowed. After several places experienced warmth, it finally snowed today. Flurries of snowflakes fell from the sky, landing on my disheveled hair and the fur collar of my coat. Gusts of northwesterly wind roared straight at my face. I could only bury my head deeper into my coat collar, my two frozen, red hands tucked into my sleeves. Ferries arrived every ten minutes. I don't know how many sailed past, but I patiently waited, waiting for her, that bird-like person, in the intensifying northwesterly wind.

"Today is Sunday. Her school has a day off, and I just called her. I distinctly heard her say she'd be here soon in the oriole-like voice coming from the receiver. Why does she always make me wait and never come?" I thought to myself.

A large group of people poured out of the small ferry. The little boat wheezed and slowly carried another group away. I stood alone on the dock, feeling desolate and forlorn! I shivered, feeling a chill in my soul. Seeing the rolling waves in the Huangpu River, surging wildly as large ships passed, and the restless ripples on the water's surface in the harbor, I grew fearful. I worried that the large waves would pull me into the whirlpool of the deep abyss. Minutes and seconds ticked by. I watched my watch, which told me it was twelve o'clock. I silently counted in my head; I had been waiting here for a full three hours.

A rickshaw flew from the distance. I strained my eyes, and indeed, there was a girl on the rickshaw. I suspected it was her, but as the rickshaw reached me, the puller's strong legs carried it past me with relentless speed. I began to curse the rickshaw puller for being so heartless and cruel. Why didn't he bring my girl? Even so, I didn't lose hope.

"Did something happen? Is she not coming? Isn't that too unexpected?..." I dared not think that. I hoped my thoughts were just the result of oversensitivity.

Pitter-patter, pitter-patter, the sound of leather shoes approached from behind. I believed it was her, but I still didn't dare turn around, afraid of another disappointment.

Another thirty minutes passed. I was really getting impatient. So, I walked against the wind towards the Bu's Stou sign, because she would definitely arrive on the × route bus. Patiently waiting, before long, a bus arrived, packed with a crowded mass of passengers. Peering in, I saw only dark heads. So, I craned my neck, perked up my spirits, and watched the passengers pouring out of the bus door. Alas! Where was she? Where could I find her shadow? Bus after bus arrived. Four buses, five buses. In the end, ah, I fell deeply into the bitter realm of disappointment.

Subconsciously, I slowly walked back to the dock. The wind whipped my head, causing it to ache. My limbs were frozen stiff, and my lower body felt especially weak, almost collapsing. The strange wind accompanying the waves on the river transformed the passionate heart I had maintained for an hour into one of ice. Ah! She was toying with me, letting me down. So, I resolutely bought a ticket, enduring the pain, and walked onto the ferry. I stared at the center of the river, staring at the towering waves. I drifted along the vast river with the boat, my own melancholy reaching a state of utter emptiness!

Ah! Her! Where has that bird-like person gone?

The New Bride

— Yu Gui

The flames in the fireplace surged warmly from the fire door, naturally warming the room and making one forget that it was a bitterly cold, snowy day with frozen bodies on the roads. However, our Miss Manli, sitting by the fireplace, did not find her heart warming along with the room; it was cold like a snowflake. She was silent, and it was already past midnight, almost the next day.

The light in the room was so bright, illuminating all the furniture: the new copper bed, the new wall decorations, and especially the new wedding photo. If Miss Manli could just lift her head slightly, we could easily guess from the wedding photo that she was a new bride.

Speaking of Miss Manli's reputation, she occupied a significant place in the minds of many young people. She was the queen of the girls' school, an angel-like celestial being. Regarding marriage, our Miss Manli had many virginal dreams. She rejected the attentiveness of every young man, believing herself to be a swallow soaring in the sky, not a lark that could be confined to a gilded cage. Her ideal mate was still in her beautiful dreams, yet—she had become a new bride.

Outside the window, snowflakes fell like goose feathers, and Miss Manli's heart felt as heavy as lead. She raised her head, her gaze flicking over the wedding photo. She couldn't believe that the man in a formal suit standing beside her would be the gilded cage of her life. Then, the faces of all the young men swept before her, her virginal dreams completely shattered. She resented herself for lacking courage. She could have casually chosen an attentive young man to escape from her mother's grasp, regardless of the outcome. She was destined to be a commodity, sold to you, sold to him, until her body was completely sold off. Yet—she was that man's legal wife.

Manli shook her head wildly, thinking she could cast off the chaotic thoughts, but the faces of many young men swept even more enthusiastically before her. She jumped up as if in a frenzy and threw herself onto the bed. She covered her face with her hands, her legs dangling off the edge of the bed. She didn't cry; she couldn't cry. Suddenly, the clock struck five times, hitting her heart like a hammer.

"Ah, he's not coming back!" she lamented as if complaining to the young men sweeping before her.

She sat up and laughed heartily. Naturally, Miss Manli couldn't think of anything worth laughing about at this moment, just like a newly widowed woman who cries out loud in the quiet of the night to relieve the resentment in her chest. Indeed, after laughing aloud, she recognized that she was on that new copper bed, a new bed with beautiful tassels, a new bed where she lost her virginal dreams, and also a new bed where her life's fate had been decided.

Miss Manli didn't believe for a moment that she could move from the sofa to the bed. So, she laughed again, raising her clenched fist and waving it vigorously in the air.

"I'll break free from this gilded cage!" The voice was as loud as a slogan shouted at a rally. Miss Manli was now like a fierce beast in a wild mountain, baring her claws and teeth, searching for the man in the formal suit. But in the room, besides the flames in the fireplace surging warmly from the fire door, she had no object for her pleasure.

She quickly climbed onto the chair, raised the wedding photo, and threw it into the fireplace. She laughed loudly, clapping her hands, as if she had killed the man in the formal suit.

She had won; she needed rest. She fell onto the copper bed. Instantly, countless young men's heads gathered. Miss Manli looked at the beautiful tassels. She sat up again, wanting to throw herself into their arms. She had broken through the tiger's mouth of the gilded cage. She suddenly lunged forward...

"Falling asleep at a time like this!" A rough voice, like a flying bullet, shattered her eardrums.

Opening her eyes, the man in the formal suit scowled.

Two clear tears hung from Miss Manli's eyes as she stared at the wedding photo. "You are a new bride!" The heads of countless young men mocked her.

A Small Variety Show

— Zu

The middle school students have been busy with everything for the past eight days. It turned out it's because they are holding a small variety show on Saturday. So, they were busy printing admission tickets, and others were busy writing notices. Some were practicing plays, while others were making red and green paper flowers, doing this, doing that, running east and west, busy and happy! Their thoughts converged on the small variety show that would open on Saturday night.

The reason is that the fifth graders also held such a small variety show last Saturday. Therefore, the students in the junior middle school department, not wanting to be outdone, also did the same thing. They thought: how can we, dignified middle school students, be inferior to these primary school students? So, we can conclude that the motive and origin of their organizing this variety show was to show off their middle school student status and compete with the elementary school department, although their only proclaimed purpose was to discuss academic studies and cultivate group life.

"When you see others have strengths, you should catch up and learn from them. You must not be jealous, but you should have a competitive spirit." That's what I heard teachers say to me often when I entered school, and now that I am in the position of a teacher, I say the same to my students.

The date of the fifth grade variety show was only five or six days ago, so I can still clearly remember what happened that day:

I took on the responsibility of being the class teacher of the fifth grade. At the request of the fifth-grade students, I finally planned everything for them and was able to hold an extremely small variety show with only a prototype last week. In addition to complying with the students' wishes and not disappointing them too much, the only purpose was to let them know more about common sense and the proceedings of meetings, because most of them are children of workers and lack knowledge in all aspects. Borrowing curtains and dance costumes, a small stage was built, and representatives from each grade were invited as usual (in fact, the number of people in each grade exceeded the number of representatives). When the time came, the bell rang to start the meeting. In a small classroom, only black heads could be seen. Everyone squeezed together, making the small classroom unbearably crowded. As usual, after the ceremony, the program began to perform. When the performance started, apart from the junior children who poked out their eyes and watched the stage with relish, the rest yelled out "Bravo!" in strange voices after each act, some even laughing coldly in their noses with a mocking tone. So, the noise in the room was endless. That headache-inducing thing had only passed for less than a week, and the middle school students were also busy trying to play this game. Wouldn't their result be the same?

Two Kinds of Leave

— Where to Go

Sitting in the classroom for too long, my buttocks can't help but feel sore and swollen. Looking at books for too long, my brain can't help but feel dizzy. So, I casually think about going outside for a walk, taking a look here, taking a look there, in order to relax and regulate the life of a scholar. Isn't that something that is very natural and in accordance with human feelings?

However, the school rules clearly don't take these into account. Students must not be absent from class without a reason, and absenting from class results in no credits, and no credits mean no graduation. All kinds of things restrict students from leaving school. So, isn't it also natural for students to take leave and go out for a stroll?

Taking leave should be for something. However, things like sitting for too long and getting sore buttocks are difficult for people to acknowledge. So, isn't it also a matter of not being able to help oneself to lie and say that one is sick, or that something has happened at home, and so on, and then taking that leave slip to leisurely stroll around?

Leisurely strolling around with a lie is inherently forbidden. But luckily, this is for one's own health. Because getting sore buttocks is bound to lead to ulceration, and getting dizzy too often is bound to lead to meningitis. When such disasters befall, people at most say a word of respect, or how rare it is, and other similar words of regret, but one's own self is needlessly ruined. Thinking about it, how unwise is that?

So, those who take leave for the sake of their health and go out to relax always understand the way to preserve life and know how to plan for themselves.

Politicians who sit in the court and think about and worry about the affairs of the country as if they were their own also often have this kind of health problem.

It is very common and frequent for politicians to have health problems, and there is no need to be surprised. Why? Because politicians are also people, and people are often sick.

People generally think that great people are like supermen. In fact, great people are just superior to others in terms of planning and superior to others in terms of skills, but in terms of physiology, they are just like ordinary people.

If they are like ordinary people, they will have the same health problems as ordinary people. What's more, they are so busy planning for the country and so hardworking doing things for the country. If you are busy enough and work hard enough, wouldn't you get sick?

So, isn't it also most in accordance with human feelings for politicians to reluctantly leave the court for the sake of their own health problems and take sick leave to recuperate?

Those who spare no effort to take leave and recuperate for the sake of their own health are always those who have attained the true essence of life. It is proper for us ordinary people to emulate, admire, and admire them.

Page 21

Page 22

Page 23

Xin'er (New Child)

— Wenbing

"Xin'er, Daddy is home! Hurry and get up!" The mischievous six-year-old Xin'er, not having had enough to eat for breakfast, threw himself on the ground and cried for a long time. His mother tried to coax him, but he ignored her. Scolding and hitting him didn't scare him. But the moment he heard that shout, he immediately scrambled up, covered in dust, and threw himself into his mother's arms, calling out in a childlike voice like a singing oriole:

"Mother, Daddy's home! Let's go meet him!" Xin'er jumped up impatiently, pulling on his mother's sleeve, insisting on going outside to meet his daddy.

This was Xin'er's third hope.

The first time was during the New Year. He said to his mother that he was six years old this year and wanted to have a new set of clothes made. His mother, unable to bear his pestering, simply agreed: "When March comes and the cotton is harvested, I'll definitely make them for you!" Xin'er then lived in hope, going to the fields every day to look at the cotton. When one or two branches formed buds, he would rush home, excitedly telling his mother and proposing the making of new clothes. Later, the weather was constantly drizzling, and Xin'er didn't go to see the cotton seedlings for ten days. But he heard his father always getting angry with his mother: "Damn it, with this kind of incessant rain, the cotton is all withering!" Sure enough, the ten acres of cotton fields didn't yield even two or three loads of dead, yellow flowers. As his mother sorted through them, Xin'er was still nagging her about making new clothes. His mother, annoyed, slapped him twice, and he fell to the ground crying.

Two days later, Xin'er took advantage of the good opportunity of his mother wanting him to get vaccinated against smallpox to bring up the condition of making new clothes. His mother calculated that there was absolutely no income recently, and they couldn't even afford firewood and rice every day, only relying on the new wheat that would come out in May. So, she definitely said to Xin'er: "If you get vaccinated well, and we harvest the wheat in May, I'll definitely tell Daddy to go buy cloth to make them for you." Xin'er was a bit skeptical at first, shaking his head, and said "No, no, the third time was still no. "No, no, no, what do you want?" His mother's anger flared, staring at him with round eyes. "I don't want it, make them now!" "Good boy, there's no money now. I'll definitely make them for you in May!" Xin'er was finally persuaded by his kind mother. "You must make them in May!" "I'll definitely make them for you!" Xin'er then agreed to get vaccinated.

Xin'er looked, looked, and May arrived. The weather was good, with favorable winds and rain. The yellow wheat ears swayed steadily in the wind and waves. Xin'er was truly delirious with joy.

Load after load of wheat was carried on his father's shoulders to the threshing ground. Xin'er sat on a low stool to guard against chickens and ducks coming to grab food. The wheat was threshed, piled up like a small, pot-shaped mountain. His father went to town to get someone to buy it. The wheat was sold, and the silver dollars flipped in his father's palm. Xin'er then remembered making new clothes, twisting and turning in front of his mother. His father whispered in his mother's ear: "Ah, the wheat price is so low, this little money isn't even enough to pay off the debt!" His father got angry, and his palm landed on Xin'er's face, and Xin'er cried again.

In July, Xin'er had the desire to make new clothes again. His mother said to him with a grieving heart: "Daddy has gone to town to inquire about the grain price. This time, if all twelve loads of new grain are sold, I'll definitely make a set for you!" Xin'er then hoped wholeheartedly.

Because he didn't have enough breakfast, Xin'er threw himself on the ground and cried for a long time. No matter how hard they tried to coax him, they couldn't get him to get up. "Xin'er, Daddy's home! Hurry and get up!" Only this made Xin'er scramble up at once.

Amateur Mailbox

How to Dissolve an Engagement Arranged by Parents?

Editor:

When I was a child, my parents arranged an engagement for me with Miss Yi. At first, I strongly protested, but because I lacked the ability, I had to obey my parents' arrangements. It wasn't until 1928 that I grew older and gained some knowledge, and I repeatedly protested this marriage to my parents. My parents ignored me, but a year later, the Yi family unfortunately suffered a sudden misfortune, and their parents all fled to escape disaster. Miss Yi was left without anyone to care for her, so my parents brought Miss Yi to temporarily care for her. Although I repeatedly opposed this matter, it was always ineffective. My parents have been taking care of Miss Yi to this day and also know that Miss Yi has a bad temper, so they sympathize with me. However, the Yi family parents returned home in 1931, but Miss Yi still remains in our care and has always opposed the dissolution of the engagement. Now, although my parents sympathize with me, they don't know the dissolution procedures, and all the responsibility is still on my shoulders, but I also lack the ability. So, I can only ask you to guide and answer the following question:

A, Can I use the following three points as reasons for dissolving the engagement?

One, the engagement was arranged by my parents without the consent of the parties involved.

Two, Miss Yi is an old-fashioned woman, illiterate, and her temperament does not match mine.

Three, according to the current slogans of freedom of marriage, freedom of divorce, and freedom of marriage.

B, If I do not marry Miss Yi and freely declare cohabitation with Miss Bing, is this bigamy?

C, If the engagement cannot be dissolved and I publish a statement in the newspaper that I do not recognize the engagement arranged by my parents, is this effective?

D, If I publish a statement in the newspaper that I do not recognize the engagement arranged by my parents, if this method is effective, what responsibility should my parents bear?

E, If the engagement cannot be dissolved and both of us are over twenty years old, but I will never want to marry Miss Yi, will I be subject to legal restraint?

Please give me a satisfactory answer and guidance to the above questions. Completed, best wishes for your health. Jiang Yifan

Editor's Note: According to the provisions of the current Civil Code, "Engagements should be made by the parties themselves." In other words, if the engagement is not made by the male and female parties themselves, it should be invalid. So, your first reason for dissolution is valid. The second and third reasons are not valid, but having the first reason is enough, and there is no need to raise the second and third reasons. Dissolving an engagement requires "filing a lawsuit." If you just publish a statement in the newspaper, I'm afraid it doesn't comply with the procedures. As for your letter's item B, the so-called "freely declaring cohabitation with Miss Bing" is not allowed by law because, before the previous engagement is dissolved, this behavior is illegal. Regarding what responsibility your parents should bear after you dissolve the engagement, according to the main points of the judgment in the case of dissolving an engagement and returning betrothal gifts in the twentieth year (Shang Zi No. 1377), "If parents, based on the power of arranging marriages under the old law, arrange an engagement for their young children, according to the principle of freedom of marriage, if one of their children, after reaching adulthood, is unwilling to fulfill the engagement, they may sue for dissolution, but in the contracting parties, they should not be allowed to change their minds without reason." So, if your parents do not meet the conditions for dissolution prescribed by the Civil Code, they cannot dissolve the engagement without reason. However, "Engagements cannot be forced to be fulfilled" is also clearly stipulated by law. If you insist on dissolving the engagement, it is not impossible, but the other party has "the right to claim damages." There are no special provisions in the law for the E item method, but it allows the other party to dissolve the engagement and claim damages.

In short, this type of incident should be resolved by law, so you must consult a lawyer for all detailed procedures.

Mao Gege and Bao Meimei Travel the World

— Meng

Novel

Manli's Freedom (6)

— Manzhi

You don't need to argue. Do you think running away from your family marriage makes you a progressive figure in the revolution? Since the May Fourth Movement, countless men and women have run away from family marriages. That was just a relic of the family revolution in the initial social movement, not some great action or glorious history. After the May Fourth Movement, the female youths who came out of family revolutions now have three different situations and ideologies. One type struggled and advanced, and now, as virtuous wives and good mothers, they are subdued in their small families. Another type breathed in new ideas at the time and embarked on the revolutionary path, but now, if they haven't died, they've become dejected and pessimistic, indulging in pleasure, detesting the family, and feeling nihilistic about life. || These people are living a slow suicide. There is also a type that held the ambition of economic independence and independent living at the time, and most studied medicine and obstetrics, followed by teaching. Now, as doctors or teachers, their lives are indeed independent, but their youth has passed like flowing water. The pain of being an old maid is only known to themselves.

You are a youth who awakened during the May Thirtieth Movement era, but you only have a simple mind. Therefore, after you came out of the family revolution, you simply struggled for your own future. Therefore, you don't understand political thought, and you hate politics. Therefore, you don't understand the suffering that great figures experience because of political thought. Therefore, you are worried and uneasy, and you cannot live with him and left him.

Manli, this is your mistake!

Now that you've left him, do you feel no regret at all? Do you feel no pain at all? "No, no, although my body has left him, my heart is still thinking of him, and my soul is often flying to find him!" You must tell me this. You must be even more buried in the thick fog of worry and unease!

Manli, then, you should think about your own mistakes: Why didn't you try to understand him?

Do you understand now? The only reason you don't understand him is that your thinking is outdated!

Also, you only see yourself. Apart from yourself, you can't even see your lover. This is naturally your uniqueness, your pride, but also your sorrow. Self-esteem is certainly precious, but self-esteem that expands to infinity becomes a distorted person who is arrogant and self-centered! Extreme individualists, especially women, find it difficult to live happily in modern society!

Don't dream that as long as you work hard and have authority and money, a lover is not a problem. Love, of course, can be plundered with authority, and can also be bought with money, but what you get is not a lover, but a human captive!

You must also remember: New people are not as good as old people, and the first person you love will never be forgotten!

However, if you repent, it is already too late!

Since Renjie came out of the hospital, his temperament, will, thoughts, and concepts have all changed completely.

After a long rain, there will be sunshine. He is precisely a barometer.

That day, I went to find him—the house where you lived—the first thing that surprised me was that he was slow in his movements, looked old, and didn't like to talk much; and from the original expression of indignation, he had lost his disappointment and gained optimism. He had become a resolute and brave warrior.
